label shall be in effect as fully as if set forth in detail in this section,
and such minimum sanitary requirements are declared to be absolute and
compulsory.
   B.   Grade A Pasteurized Milk Or Milk Products Only:
      1.   No person shall sell, offer for sale, or deliver any milk or milk
products to any final consumer within the city except grade A pasteurized milk
or grade A pasteurized milk products which are so labeled.
      2.   No person shall sell, offer for sale, or deliver any raw milk to any
consumer, whether for human consumption or animal consumption, within the city.
   C.   Examination Of Milk And Milk Products:
      1.   The director of public health shall be authorized to take and
examine samples of milk and milk products from any person as often as he deems
necessary for the protection of the public health.
      2.   All proprietors of hotels, hospitals, food service establishments,
retail food stores, and other similar establishments shall furnish the
director, upon his request, the names of all distributors from whom their milk
and milk products are obtained. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
 
Notes
1 1. 410 ILCS 635/1 et seq.
4-1D-3: FOOD SERVICE ESTABLISHMENTS AND RETAIL FOOD STORES:
   A.   Certificate Required: No food service establishment or retail food
store shall be issued a food service establishment license, itinerant food
service establishment license, mobile food service establishment license or
retail food store license pursuant to the provisions of this article unless it
has been inspected by the director of public health or a designated
representative, it has been determined that the food service establishment
complies with all the requirements of this article, and the food service
establishment or retail food store has been issued a certificate to operate.
   B.   Display Of Certificate: The certificate issued pursuant to this section
shall be displayed in a conspicuous public place in the food service
establishment or retail food store before such food service establishment or
retail food store can be considered to be in compliance with this article.
   C.   Renewal Of Certificate: Food service establishment or retail food store
certificates shall be renewed every six (6) months following an inspection by
the department. In the event the inspection for the renewal of a certificate
reveals the existence of any emergency health hazard or any health hazard, or
repeated violations of this article, the certificate will not be renewed, and
the department shall notify the certificate holder immediately thereof. Such
notice shall state the reasons for nonrenewal of the certificate and shall also
state that an opportunity for a hearing, pursuant to the requirements of this
section, shall be granted. This notice shall be delivered to the certificate
holder in person or may be sent by certified mail.
   D.   New Certificate Required After Voluntary Closing: If a food service
establishment or retail food store ceases operation for one month or longer for
any reason, a new certificate must be obtained before the food service
establishment or retail food store may be reopened. If ownership of the food
service establishment or retail food store changes, the new operator may not
open the food service establishment or retail food store until a new
certificate and new license are obtained pursuant to the procedures set forth
in this article.
   E.   Inspections:
      1.   At least once every six (6) months, an environmental health
inspector shall inspect each food service establishment or retail food store
and shall make as many additional inspections and reinspections as are
necessary for the enforcement of this article. The environmental health
inspector, after proper identification, shall be permitted to enter at any time
during business hours any food service establishment or retail food store for
the purpose of making inspections to determine compliance with this article. In
case of suspected or verified food borne disease outbreaks, the environmental
health inspector shall be permitted to examine the records of the food service
establishment or retail food store which contain pertinent information relative
to persons employed and food and supplies purchased, received or used.
      2.   The environmental health inspector shall record all findings on an
inspection report form provided for this purpose and shall furnish a copy of
such inspection report form to the certificate holder at the time of
inspection.
      3.   Whenever the environmental health inspector discovers that any of
the requirements of this article have been violated, he shall notify the
certificate holder or food service establishment or retail food store manager
of such violations by means of the inspection report form or other written
notice from the department. In such notification, the environmental health
inspector shall:
         a.   Set forth the specific violation found.
         b.   Establish a specific and reasonable period of time for the
correction of the violations found.
         c.   State that failure to comply with any notice issued in accordance
with the provisions of this article may result in immediate suspension of the
certificate.
         d.   State that an opportunity for appeal from any notice or
inspection findings will be provided if a written request for a hearing is
filed with the director within the period of time established in the notice of
correction.
      4.   Notices provided for under this section shall be deemed to have been
properly served when the original copy of the inspection report form or other
notice has been delivered personally or by certified mail, addressee only, to
the certificate holder or manager of the food service establishment or retail
food store. A copy of such notice shall be filed with the records of the
department.
   F.   Examination And Condemnation Of Food:
      1.   Food may be examined or requested for analysis by the department as
often as may be necessary to determine freedom from adulteration or
misbranding. The director may, on written notice to the certificate holder or
the food service establishment or retail food store manager, place a hold order
on any food which is determined to be unwholesome or otherwise adulterated or
misbranded. Under a hold order, food shall be permitted to remain on the
premises; provided, that it is suitably stored and not served.
      2.   No person shall remove or alter a hold order notice or tag placed on
food or on the food service establishment or retail food store by
representatives of the department, and neither such food nor the containers
thereof shall be relabeled, repacked, reprocessed, altered, disposed of, or
destroyed without permission of the director, except on order by a court of
competent jurisdiction. After the certificate holder or food service
establishment or retail food store manager has had a hearing as provided for in
this section, and on the basis of evidence produced at such hearing, or on the
basis of an examination in the event a written request for a hearing is not
received within ten (10) days, the director may vacate the hold order or may,
by written order, direct the certificate holder or food service establishment
manager or retail food store manager of the food which was placed under the
hold order to destroy such food or bring it into compliance with the provisions
of this article.
   G.   Establishments Outside Jurisdiction Of Department: When food from food
service establishments or retail food stores outside the jurisdiction of the
department is sold within the jurisdiction of the department, such food service
establishments or retail food stores should conform to the provisions of this
article or to equivalent provisions of another jurisdiction. To determine the
extent of compliance with such provision, the department may accept reports
from responsible authorities in other jurisdictions where such food service
establishments or retail food stores are located.
   H.   Suspension Of Certificate; Reinstatement:
      1.   Temporary Suspension:
         a.   Food service establishment and retail food store certificates may
be suspended temporarily by the director for failure of the certificate holder
to continue to comply with the requirements of this article.
         b.   Whenever a certificate holder has failed to comply with any
notice issued under the provisions of this section, the certificate holder
shall be notified in writing that the certificate is, upon service of the
notice, immediately suspended, and that an opportunity for a hearing will be
provided pursuant to this section. Whenever alleged violations of this article
constitute an emergency health hazard, the director shall issue a written
notice to the certificate holder citing such conditions, specifying the
corrective action to be taken and specifying the time period within which such
action shall be taken, and if deemed necessary, such order may state that the
certificate is immediately suspended, and all operations as a food service
establishment or retail food store are to be immediately discontinued.
         c.   Any person to whom such an order is issued shall comply
immediately therewith but, on written application to the director, shall be
afforded a hearing as soon as possible, but in no event, later than two (2)
working days after issuance of the order.
         d.   The city attorney shall be notified of each food service
establishment or retail food store that has had its certificate to operate
suspended and shall enforce that ruling.
      2.   Reinstatement Of Suspended Certificate: Any person whose food
service establishment or retail food store certificate has been suspended by
the director may make an application for the purpose of reinstatement of the
certificate. Reinspection shall be made by the director or his representative
on the next working day following receipt of a written request which shall
include a statement signed by the certificate holder that, in his opinion,
conditions causing suspension of the certificate have been corrected. If the
former certificate holder is in compliance with the requirements of this
article, the certificate shall be reinstated.
   I.   Hearings: Any person affected by an order or notice issued by the
director or a designee in connection with the enforcement of any provision of
this article pertaining to food service establishments or retail food stores
may file in the office of the director a written petition for a hearing by the
director. The director or a designee shall hold a hearing at a time and place
designated by him within fifteen (15) days of the date on which the written
petition was filed. The petitioner shall be notified of the time and place of
the hearing not less than five (5) working days prior to the date on which the
hearing is to be held. If, as a result of the hearing, the director or a
designee finds that strict compliance with the order or notices would cause
undue hardship on the petitioner, and that the public health would be protected
by varying or withdrawing the order or notice and, as a condition for such
action, may, where he deems necessary, make requirements which are additional
to those prescribed in this article for the purpose of protecting the public
health. The director or a designee shall render a decision in writing within
ten (10) days after the date of the hearing and place a copy of the decision on
file in the office of the director as a matter of public record. (Ord. 225, 3-
25-1985)
ARTICLE E.  GARBAGE, RUBBISH, SOLID WASTE AND WEEDS
SECTION:
4-1E-1: Accumulation Of Garbage And Rubbish Prohibited
4-1E-2: Removal Of Garbage, Rubbish, Solid Waste And Weeds Required
4-1E-3: Garbage Receptacles
4-1E-4: Burning Garbage And Rubbish
4-1E-5: Unlawful Deposits
4-1E-6: Exemptions From Provisions
4-1E-7: Tree Limb And Branch Pick Up Program
4-1E-1: ACCUMULATION OF GARBAGE AND RUBBISH PROHIBITED:
No person shall allow or cause the accumulation of garbage or rubbish except as
provided in this article, nor allow or cause any vehicles containing garbage or
rubbish to remain on or along any railroad, street, or highway in the city.
(Ord. 225, 3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
4-1E-2: REMOVAL OF GARBAGE, RUBBISH, SOLID WASTE AND WEEDS REQUIRED:
   A.   Garbage And Rubbish: The owner, occupant, lessee or contract for deed
buyer of any premises shall remove or have removed from his premises any
garbage and rubbish at least once each week.
   B.   Brush, Trees, Stumps And Solid Waste: The owner, occupant, lessee or
contract for deed buyer of any premises shall remove or have removed from his
premises any brush, dead or dying trees, stumps, roots, or solid waste
material. The removal shall be performed within ten (10) days after receipt by
the owner, occupant, lessee, contract for deed buyer, or his agent of a public
health violation ticket; provided, that the removal of solid waste material
shall be performed within three (3) days after receipt of the ticket. (Ord.
225, 3-25-1985)
   C.   Weeds: The owner, occupant, lessee or contract for deed buyer of any
premises shall remove or have removed from his premises any rank growth of
weeds. The removal shall be performed within five (5) days after receipt of
notice. The notice shall also contain a statement that failure to remove the
rank growth of weeds within five (5) days may result in the city itself, under
the direction of the department of public health, correcting the violation, or
the filing of an ordinance violation that may result, upon conviction, in a
fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code for each day the violation continues, or both. Service of
the notice shall be made by regular mail with one copy delivered to the city
attorney and one copy retained by the department of public health. (Ord. 225,
3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
4-1E-3: GARBAGE RECEPTACLES:
   A.   Required; Specifications:
      1.   The owner or occupant of any single-family residence or multiple-
dwelling residence with less than four (4) dwelling units shall provide, or
cause to be provided, and shall maintain clean and in good repair, a receptacle
or receptacles that are:
         a.   Galvanized metal or plastic with a close fitting metal or plastic
cover.
         b.   Watertight.
         c.   A capacity of not less than five (5) nor more than thirty five
(35) gallons.
         d.   With suitable handles for carrying.
         e.   Sufficient to contain the accumulation of waste material for a
period of at least seven (7) days.
      2.   In all cases, it shall be the ultimate responsibility of the owner
to provide the proper receptacles for the premises.
   B.   Use Required: It shall be the duty of every owner or occupant of any
premises to dispose of any garbage and rubbish in receptacles described in this
article. The removal of any garbage or rubbish shall be accomplished in a
manner which does not create a nuisance or cause annoyance or discomfort to any
person.
   C.   Placement For Collection: All receptacles for the collection of garbage
and rubbish shall be placed on the owner's premises in an accessible place at
ground level. No receptacle shall be placed on public property or right of way
so as to impede or interfere with pedestrian or motor vehicle traffic. (Ord.
225, 3-25-1985)
   D.   Unlawful Use:
      1.   The removal of any garbage or rubbish from any receptacle for any
purpose while awaiting its collection is prohibited, unless the removal is by
the owner or occupant of the premises on which the receptacle belongs. (Ord.
225, 3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
      2.   The tipping over of any receptacle provided for the placement of
garbage or rubbish, or the removal of any cover from a receptacle without
replacement in its proper position, is prohibited. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
4-1E-4: BURNING GARBAGE AND RUBBISH 1 :
No person shall burn or cause to be burned any garbage or rubbish in the city.
(Ord. 225, 3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also chapter 3 of this title.
4-1E-5: UNLAWFUL DEPOSITS 1 :
   A.   No person shall deposit, collect, or transport garbage or rubbish in
such a manner that it may be spread by natural elements, such as wind or rain,
or by animals onto any premises.
   B.   No person shall deposit garbage or rubbish on any public place. This
subsection shall not apply to goods or merchandise deposited on a public place
pursuant to a permit authorized by ordinance of the city if the goods or
merchandise are removed from the public place within two (2) hours after having
been deposited, or to articles deposited in the city sewage system through
lawful drains in accordance with this chapter. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
 
Notes
1 2. See also section
  7-1-1 of this code.
4-1E-6: EXEMPTIONS FROM PROVISIONS:
Nothing contained in this article shall be construed to apply to persons hired
or employed for the purpose of collecting garbage or rubbish and disposing
thereof; however, all receptacles shall be replaced after collection in an
upright position with the covers on them. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
4-1E-7: TREE LIMB AND BRANCH PICK UP PROGRAM:
   A.   The city of Leland Grove shall provide for the pick up and removal of
tree limbs and branches from residences in the city for property located within
the city's geographic boundaries. The pick up will be conducted on the first
Monday of every month and shall begin in the city ward as is determined on a
rotating basis by need.
   B.   Tree limbs and branches which are eligible to be included in the city's
pick up program must consist of branches and limbs less than two inches (2") in
diameter and must be placed in a residential sized receptacle for garbage or
trash. All bushes must have the root ball removed and be in pieces smaller than
two feet (2') in diameter and six feet (6') in length. The owner of the subject
property must perform all work on the property and no material may be moved
from any other property into the city or from one property to another property
within the city.
   C.   The volume of limbs and branches picked up at any one time shall be
limited to one pile no more than six feet (6') long by six feet (6') wide by
six feet (6') tall. Any item of less than one-half inch (1/2") in diameter must
be placed in a yard waste bag, with the appropriate sticker and disposed of by
a licensed waste hauler at the property owner's expense. The property owner may
request that additional limbs and branches be removed for the requisite fee, as
established from time to time by the city at the direction of the mayor,
subject to the city's ability and availability to remove any additional limbs
or branches.
   D.   The following items will not be eligible for the pick up program:
      1.   Leaves, grass clippings, weeds, and other yard waste.
      2.   Whole bushes, vines and hedge trimmings.
      3.   Compost material.
      4.   Roots.
      5.   Tree limbs larger than eight inches (8") in diameter.
      6.   Whole trees.
      7.   Any paper or plastic bag or other nonorganic matter.
   E.   The tree limbs and branches must be located on the city right of way
directly in front of the subject property, but shall not be located on the
pavement portion of any street or on any other city property. Any material
shall not be placed in the right of way earlier than the Saturday prior to the
scheduled pick up date. (Ord. 368, 2-22-2011)
ARTICLE F.  HOUSING STANDARDS
SECTION:
4-1F-1: Minimum Standards For Equipment And Facilities
4-1F-2: Minimum Standards For Light, Ventilation, Heat And Pest Control
4-1F-3: General Requirements For Safe And Sanitary Maintenance
4-1F-4: Minimum Space, Use And Location Requirements
4-1F-5: Responsibilities Of Owners And Occupants
4-1F-6: Dwellings Unfit For Human Habitation
4-1F-7: Enforcement
4-1F-1: MINIMUM STANDARDS FOR EQUIPMENT AND FACILITIES:
All dwellings or dwelling units, or any portion thereof, that are used,
designed, or intended to be used for human habitation shall meet the following
requirements:
   A.   Water And Sewer Utilities:
      1.   All fixtures in such dwelling or dwelling unit required by the
provisions of subsections B1, B2 and B3 of this section shall be properly
installed and connected to a public sewer.
      2.   If a water main is located in, over, or under the lot or land on
which a dwelling or dwelling unit is situated or such water main is located in
a street or alley abutting such lot or land, all fixtures in such dwelling or
dwelling unit required by the provisions of this section shall be properly
installed and connected to such water main.
   B.   Sanitary Facilities:
      1.   Every dwelling or dwelling unit shall contain a kitchen sink in good
working condition and properly connected to an approved water and sewer system
in compliance with this article.
      2.   Every dwelling or dwelling unit shall contain, within a room which
affords privacy to a person within the room, a flush water closet and a
lavatory basin in good working condition and properly connected to an approved
water and sewer system in compliance with this article.
      3.   Every dwelling or dwelling unit shall contain, within a room which
affords privacy to a person within the room, a bathtub or shower in good
working condition and properly connected to an approved water and sewer system.
      4.   Every kitchen sink, lavatory basin, and bathtub or shower required
under the provisions of subsections B1, B2 and B3 of this section shall be
properly connected with hot and cold water lines.
   C.   Garbage And Rubbish Storage Facilities: Every dwelling or dwelling unit
shall be supplied with adequate garbage and rubbish storage facilities.
   D.   Exits:
      1.   Every dwelling or dwelling unit shall have safe, unobstructed means
of egress leading to safe and open space at ground level, as required by the
laws of the state and this article.
      2.   Every dwelling containing two (2) or more dwelling units shall
provide at least two (2) means of egress leading to safe and open space at
ground level from each story above the first story.
   E.   Water Heating Facilities: Every dwelling or dwelling unit shall be
supplied with water heating facilities which are properly installed, are
maintained in safe and good working condition, are properly connected with the
hot water lines required under the provisions of this article and are capable
of heating water to such temperature as to permit an adequate amount of water
to be drawn at every required kitchen sink, lavatory basin, bathtub, or shower
at a temperature of not less than one hundred twenty degrees Fahrenheit
(120°F).
   F.   Signage: Every residence or dwelling unit shall have the numerical
street number visible from a distance of twenty feet (20') and visible from the
street, in a size of not less than three inches (3") in height and in a color
contrasting to that of the surface on which they are placed on the residence or
dwelling unit. (Ord. 382, 2-26-2013)
4-1F-2: MINIMUM STANDARDS FOR LIGHT, VENTILATION, HEAT AND PEST CONTROL:
All dwellings or dwelling units, or any portion thereof, that are used, or
designed or intended to be used, for human habitation shall meet the following
requirements:
   A.   Light And Ventilation:
      1.   Every habitable room shall have at least one window or skylight
facing directly to the outdoors. The minimum total window area, measured
between stops, for every habitable room shall be ten percent (10%) of the floor
area of such room. Whenever walls or other portions of structures face a window
of any such room and such light obstructing structures are located less than
three feet (3') from the window and extend to a level above that of the ceiling
of the room, such a window shall not be deemed to face directly to the outdoors
and shall not be included as contributing to the required minimum total window
area. Whenever the only window in a room is a skylight type window in the top
of such room, the total window area of such skylight shall equal at least
fifteen percent (15%) of the total floor area of such room.
      2.   Every habitable room shall have at least one window or skylight
which can easily be opened, or such other device as will adequately ventilate
the room. The total of openable window area in every habitable room shall be
equal to at least forty five percent (45%) of the minimum window area size or
minimum skylight type window size as required in subsection A1 of this section,
except where there is supplied some other device affording adequate ventilation
and approved by an environmental health inspector.
      3.   Every bathroom and water closet compartment shall comply with the
light and ventilation requirements for habitable rooms contained in subsections
A1 and A2 of this section; except, that no window or skylight shall be required
in adequately ventilated bathrooms and water closet compartments equipped with
a mechanical ventilation system capable of exhausting twenty five (25) cubic
feet of air per minute which is kept in operating condition and approved by an
environmental health inspector.
      4.   Where there is an electric power line available in a street, alley,
or utility easement abutting the lot or land on which a dwelling is situated,
or such line is available over or under such lot or land, every habitable room
of such dwelling shall contain at least two (2) convenience outlets, or one
such convenience outlet and one supplied ceiling type electric light fixture;
and every water closet compartment, bathroom, laundry room, furnace room,
public hall, and stairway shall contain at least one supplied ceiling or wall
type electric light fixture. Every such outlet and fixture shall be properly
installed, shall be maintained in good and safe working condition, and shall be
connected to the source of electric power in conformance with this article.
      5.   Every public hall and stairway in every multiple dwelling containing
four (4) or more dwelling units shall be adequately lighted at all times. Every
public hall and stairway in structures devoted solely to dwelling occupancy and
containing not more than three (3) dwelling units may be supplied with
conveniently located light switches controlling an adequate lighting system
which may be turned on when needed instead of full time lighting.
   B.   Heat: Every dwelling unit shall have heating facilities which are
properly installed, maintained in a safe and good working condition, and
capable of safely and adequately heating every habitable room, bathroom, and
toilet compartment in every dwelling to a temperature of at least sixty eight
degrees Fahrenheit (68°F) every day other than during the period from May 15
through October 14, inclusive, in each year. The temperature shall be read at a
height of three feet (3') above floor level at any point in the room more than
two feet (2') from the inside of any exterior wall.
   C.   Insect And Rodent Control 1 :
      1.   From May 1 to November 1, every door opening directly from a
dwelling unit to outdoor space shall be supplied with screens and a self-
closing device, and every window or other device with openings to outdoor space
used or intended to be used for ventilation shall likewise be supplied with
screens as a protection against mosquitoes, flies, and other insects.
      2.   Every basement or cellar window used or intended to be used for
ventilation and every other opening to a basement which might provide an entry
for rodents shall be supplied with a screen or such other device as will
effectively prevent their entrance. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
 
Notes
1 1. See also article H of this chapter.
4-1F-3: GENERAL REQUIREMENTS FOR SAFE AND SANITARY MAINTENANCE:
All dwellings or dwelling units, or any portion thereof, that are used, or
designed or intended to be used, for human habitation shall meet the following
requirements:
   A.   Every foundation, floor, wall, ceiling, and roof shall be reasonably
weathertight, watertight, and rodentproof; shall be capable of affording
privacy; and shall be kept in sound condition and good repair.
   B.   Every window, exterior door, and basement hatchway shall be reasonably
weathertight, watertight, and rodentproof and shall be kept in sound working
condition and good repair.
   C.   Every inside and outside stair, every porch, and every appurtenance
thereto shall be so constructed as to be safe to use and capable of supporting
the load that normal use may cause to be placed thereon, and shall be kept in
sound condition and good repair.
   D.   Every door available as an exit shall be capable of being opened from
the inside and without the use of a key. Hasp locks are prohibited.
   E.   Every exterior door, door hinge, and door latch shall be in good
condition and shall fit reasonably well within its frame when closed.
   F.   In every dwelling or multiple dwelling, every water line, plumbing
fixture, drain, and every stack, waste and sewer line shall be so installed and
maintained as to function properly and be kept free from obstructions, leaks,
and defects.
   G.   Every water closet compartment floor surface and bathroom floor surface
shall be constructed and maintained so as to be reasonably impervious to water
and so as to permit such floor to be kept in a clean and sanitary condition.
   H.   Every supplied facility, piece of equipment or utility which is
required under this section shall be so constructed or installed that it will
function safely and effectively and shall be maintained in satisfactory working
condition.
   I.   No owner, operator, or occupant shall cause any service, facility,
equipment, or utility, which is required under this section, to be removed from
or shut off from or discontinued for any occupied dwelling let or occupied by
him, except for such temporary interruption as may be necessary while actual
repairs or alterations are in process.
   J.   No owner shall occupy or let to any other occupant any vacant dwelling
unit unless it is clean, sanitary, and fit for human occupancy. (Ord. 225, 3-
25-1985)
4-1F-4: MINIMUM SPACE, USE AND LOCATION REQUIREMENTS:
All dwellings or dwelling units, or any portion thereof, that are used, or
designed or intended to be used, for human habitation shall meet the following
requirements:
   A.   Every dwelling unit shall contain at least one hundred fifty (150)
square feet of floor space for the first occupant thereof and at least one
hundred (100) additional square feet of floor space for every additional
occupant thereof, the floor space to be calculated on the basis of total
habitable room area.
   B.   In every dwelling unit of two (2) or more rooms, every room occupied
for sleeping purposes by one occupant shall contain at least seventy (70)
square feet of floor space, and every room occupied for sleeping purposes by
more than one occupant shall contain at least fifty (50) square feet of floor
space for each occupant thereof.
   C.   No dwelling containing two (2) or more dwelling units shall have such
room arrangements that access to a bathroom or water closet compartment can be
had only by going through another dwelling unit, nor shall room arrangements be
such that access to a sleeping room can be had only by going through another
dwelling unit.
   D.   At least one-half (1/2) of the floor area of every habitable room shall
have a ceiling height of at least seven feet (7'), and the floor area of that
part of any room where the ceiling height is less than five feet (5') shall not
be considered as part of the floor area in computing the total floor area of
the room for the purpose of determining the maximum permissible occupancy
thereof.
   E.   No basement space shall be used as a habitable room or dwelling unit
unless:
      1.   The floor and walls are protected against leakage of underground and
surface runoff water and are protected against dampness;
      2.   The total window area in each room is equal to the minimum window
area sizes as required in this article;
      3.   Such required minimum window area is located entirely above the
grade of the ground adjoining such window area;
      4.   The total openable window area in each room is equal to the minimum
as required under this article; and
      5.   All window safety bar obstructions are prohibited and must be
removed unless designed and constructed so as to break away from the inside or
have latches that allow them to be opened from the inside.
   F.   No cellar space shall be used as a habitable room or dwelling unit.
(Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
4-1F-5: RESPONSIBILITIES OF OWNERS AND OCCUPANTS:
   A.   Every owner of a dwelling containing two (2) or more dwelling units
shall be responsible for maintaining, in a clean and sanitary condition, the
shared or public areas of the dwelling and premises.
   B.   Every occupant of a dwelling or dwelling unit shall keep, in a clean
and sanitary condition, that part of the dwelling, dwelling unit and premises
which he occupies and controls.
   C.   Every occupant of a dwelling or dwelling unit shall dispose of all
garbage and rubbish in a clean and sanitary manner by placing it in the
containers required by this article.
   D.   The owner or occupant of any single-family residence or multiple-
dwelling residence with less than four (4) dwelling units shall provide, or
cause to be provided, and shall maintain clean and in good repair, a receptacle
or receptacles as provided this article.
   E.   Every occupant of a dwelling or dwelling unit shall be responsible for
hanging all screens whenever the same is required under the provisions of this
article or of any rule or regulation adopted pursuant hereto, except where the
owner has agreed to supply such service. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
   F.   Every occupant of a dwelling containing a single dwelling unit shall be
responsible for the extermination of any insects, rodents, or other pests
therein or on the premises, and every occupant of a dwelling unit in a dwelling
containing more than one dwelling unit shall be responsible for such
extermination whenever his dwelling unit is the only one infested.
Notwithstanding the foregoing provisions of this subsection, whenever
infestation is caused by failure of the owner to maintain a dwelling in a
pestproof or reasonably pestproof condition, extermination shall be the
responsibility of the owner. Whenever infestation exists in two (2) or more of
the dwelling units in any dwelling or in the shared or public parts of any
dwelling containing two (2) or more dwelling units, extermination thereof shall
be the responsibility of the owner. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
   G.   Every occupant of a dwelling unit shall keep all plumbing fixtures
therein in a clean and sanitary condition and shall be responsible for the
exercise of reasonable care in the proper use and operation thereof. (Ord. 225,
3-25-1985)
4-1F-6: DWELLINGS UNFIT FOR HUMAN HABITATION:
The designation of dwellings or dwelling units as unfit for human habitation
and the procedure for the determination and placarding of such unfit dwellings
or dwelling units shall be carried out in compliance with the following
requirements:
   A.   Determination Of Unfit Dwellings: Any dwelling or dwelling unit which
shall be found to have any of the following defects shall be declared as unfit
for human habitation and shall be so designated and placarded by the
environmental health inspector:
      1.   One which is so damaged, decayed, dilapidated, unsanitary, unsafe,
or vermin infested that it creates a serious hazard to the health or safety of
the occupants or of the public.
      2.   One which lacks illumination, ventilation, or sanitation facilities
adequate to protect the health or safety of the occupants or of the public.
      3.   One which, because of its general condition or location, is
unsanitary or otherwise dangerous to the health or safety of the occupants or
of the public.
   B.   Premises Placarded And Vacated: Any dwelling or dwelling unit
determined as unfit for human habitation, and so designated and placarded by
the environmental health inspector, shall be vacated within a reasonable time
as ordered by the environmental health inspector.
   C.   Approval For Use Of Placarded Premises: No dwelling or dwelling unit
which has been determined and placarded as unfit for human habitation shall
again be used for human habitation until written approval is secured from, and
such placard is removed by, the environmental health inspector. The
environmental health inspector shall remove such placard only when the defects
on which the determination and placarding action were based have been
eliminated and after the dwelling or dwelling unit has been inspected and been
found to comply in all respects with the requirements of this article.
   D.   Tampering With Placard Prohibited: No person shall deface or remove the
placard from any dwelling or dwelling unit which has been determined as unfit
for human habitation and placarded as such, except as provided in subsection C
of this section. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
4-1F-7: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Notice Of Violation: Whenever the director or a designee has determined
that any premises fails to meet the requirements set forth in this article or
in applicable rules and regulations promulgated pursuant hereto, he shall issue
a notice setting forth the alleged failures and advising the owner or occupant
that such failures must be corrected. This notice shall:
      1.   Be in writing;
      2.   Set forth the alleged violations of any applicable ordinance, rule,
or regulation;
      3.   Describe the dwelling or dwelling unit where the violations are
alleged to exist;
      4.   Specify a reasonable time limit for the correction of any violation
alleged; and
      5.   Be served on the owner or occupant of the dwelling or dwelling unit
personally, or by certified mail. If one or more persons to whom such notice is
addressed cannot be found after diligent effort to do so, service may be made
on such persons by posting the notice in or about the dwelling unit described
in the notice.
   B.   Inspections: At the end of the period of time allowed for the
correction of any violation alleged, an environmental health inspector shall
inspect the dwelling or dwelling unit described in the notice.
   C.   Remedies: If, on inspection, the violations are determined not to have
been corrected, legal proceedings may be initiated for the immediate correction
of the alleged violations, or other appropriate action may be taken. (Ord. 225,
3-25-1985)
ARTICLE G.  LEAD AND TOXIC SUBSTANCES
SECTION:
4-1G-1: Use Restricted
4-1G-2: Labeling Requirements
4-1G-3: Responsibility Of Public Health Officials
4-1G-4: Responsibility Of Owner
4-1G-5: Prohibited Eviction Of Occupants
4-1G-6: Reporting Requirements
4-1G-1: USE RESTRICTED:
No person shall use or apply lead bearing substances or toxic heavy metal based
coatings in or on any surface of any dwelling or dwelling unit. (Ord. 225, 3-
25-1985)
4-1G-2: LABELING REQUIREMENTS:
Containers in which lead bearing substances or toxic heavy metal based coatings
are stored, sold, transferred, or added for wholesale or retail purposes shall
be labeled in conformance with state and federal laws, regulations and
recommended standards set forth in the federal hazardous substance labeling
act, as enacted and amended. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
4-1G-3: RESPONSIBILITY OF PUBLIC HEALTH OFFICIALS:
   A.   The director or his designee may inspect surfaces of dwellings or
dwelling units for the purpose of determining the presence of lead bearing
substances, and the director or his designee may cause testing to be performed
on the surfaces to determine whether or not they are in sound condition.
   B.   If, on inspection by the director or his designee, there is found to be
the presence of flaking, peeling, or loose paint, plaster, or any other
structural material on a surface in or around any dwelling or dwelling unit,
the director or his designee is empowered to take samples and to analyze or
have the samples analyzed to determine whether or not the material contains
substances prohibited by this article. In lieu of taking samples, the surface
may be tested by such method as is approved by the director or a designee.
   C.   In those cases where analysis reveals the presence of any lead bearing
substance, the director or his designee shall notify the owner in writing of
the conditions and may order the owner to remove all articles containing any
lead bearing substance or to cover such substances with an acceptable covering.
All coverings shall be securely attached to a smooth, sound surface and shall
be in accordance with existing building codes. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
4-1G-4: RESPONSIBILITY OF OWNER:
The owner shall be required to make the necessary repairs to eliminate the lead
hazard within ten (10) days from the date of receipt of the notice sent by the
director or his designee pursuant to the provisions of this chapter. It shall
be a violation of this section if the owner fails to make such necessary
repairs in a specified time. The director or his designee may extend the time
required to perform the necessary repairs to eliminate the lead hazard for a
period not to exceed thirty (30) days if the owners demonstrate a good faith
effort to make these repairs and some temporary repairs have been made to
alleviate any imminent danger caused by the lead hazard. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
4-1G-5: PROHIBITED EVICTION OF OCCUPANTS:
No owner found to be in violation of any provision contained in this article
shall evict or cause to be evicted or terminate the tenancy of a renter or
lessee for the purpose of avoiding corrective maintenance orders by the
director, court, or other appropriate authority. Occupants shall be permitted
to continue their occupancy in accordance with their lease or rental agreement
executed prior to corrective maintenance orders. Eviction or termination of
tenancy solely as retaliation for corrective maintenance shall be prohibited.
Eviction of tenants with dependent children and subsequent rental or leasing to
adult occupants only shall not constitute compliance with this article. (Ord.
225, 3-25-1985)
4-1G-6: REPORTING REQUIREMENTS:
Every physician, other diagnosing person, or director of a laboratory who has
evidence of undue lead absorption in any person shall make a report thereof to
the director within three (3) days of the finding. The report shall include the
circumstances of the case and the name and address of the person involved.
(Ord. 225, 3-25-1985)
ARTICLE H.  PEST CONTROL
SECTION:
4-1H-1: Building To Be Pestproofed
4-1H-2: Notice Requirements
4-1H-3: Pestproofed Buildings
4-1H-4: Future Construction
4-1H-5: Specific Pest Control Measures
4-1H-1: BUILDING TO BE PESTPROOFED:
It is provided and required that all buildings within the jurisdiction of the
public health department shall be pestproofed and freed of pests when directed
by the director of public health or his designee or as required in this
article. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
4-1H-2: NOTICE REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Notice To Owner: Whenever the director or his designee notifies the
owner of any building in writing that there is evidence of the need for
pestproofing of the building, such owner shall take immediate measures for
pestproofing the building.
   B.   Notice To Occupant: Whenever the director or his designee notifies the
occupant of a building in writing that there is evidence of pest infestation of
the building or on the premises, such occupant shall immediately institute pest
eradication measures and shall continuously maintain such measures in a
satisfactory manner until the building or premises is pest free or the director
or his designee advises that there is no evidence of pest infestation. (Ord.
225, 3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
4-1H-3: PESTPROOFED BUILDINGS:
   A.   Maintenance Requirements: The owners of all pestproofed buildings are
required to maintain the premises in a pestproof condition and to repair all
openings or leaks that may occur in the pestproofing.
   B.   Inspections: An environmental health inspector shall make periodic
inspections of all pestproofed buildings to determine evidence of pest
infestation and the existence of new breaks or leaks in their pestproofing.
When any evidence is found indicating the presence of pests or openings through
which pests may again enter buildings, the environmental health inspector shall
serve the owners or occupants, or both, with notices of orders to abate the
conditions found.
   C.   Removal Of Pestproofing Prohibited: No occupant, owner, contractor,
utility company, plumber, repair person, or any other person shall remove the
pestproofing from any building for any purpose and fail to restore the same in
satisfactory condition or to make any new openings that are not closed or
sealed against the entrance of pests. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
4-1H-4: FUTURE CONSTRUCTION:
No person shall construct, repair, or remodel any building, unless such
construction, repair, or remodeling shall render the building pestproof,
provided that only such repairs or remodeling as affect the pestproof condition
of any such building shall be considered as subject to the provisions of this
article. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
4-1H-5: SPECIFIC PEST CONTROL MEASURES:
   A.   Food Storage: All human or animal food or feed shall be stored in pest
free and pestproof containers, compartments, or rooms.
   B.   Garbage And Rubbish Disposal: All waste material on which pests may
feed and all small dead animals shall be placed and stored in covered metal
containers of a type prescribed by this chapter until collected.
   C.   Firewood, Lumber, Boxes And Barrels: No person shall place, leave,
dump, or permit to accumulate on any private or public premises, improved or
vacant, or on any open land, street, or alley, any firewood, lumber, boxes,
barrels, bottles, cans, containers, or similar materials unless the same shall
be placed on open racks that are elevated not less than eighteen inches (18")
above the ground, and evenly piled or stacked so that these materials will not
afford harborage for pests. (Ord. 225, 3-25-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
CHAPTER 2
ABANDONED VEHICLES
SECTION:
4-2-1: Definitions
4-2-2: Abandonment Prohibited; Removal Authorized
4-2-3: Duty To Notify Police Of Abandoned, Unclaimed Vehicle
4-2-4: Abandoned, Wrecked Vehicle On Street
4-2-5: Record Of Towed Vehicles
4-2-6: Owner Unknown
4-2-7: Reclamation Of Vehicle
4-2-8: Sale And Disposal Of Vehicle
4-2-9: Disposition Of Revenue
4-2-10: Nonliability Of Police And Towing Service
4-2-11: Violation; Penalty
4-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following words shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
ABANDONED VEHICLE: Any motor vehicle or other vehicle in a state of disrepair
rendering the vehicle incapable of being driven in its condition, or any motor
vehicle or other vehicle that has not been moved or used for seven (7)
consecutive days or more and is apparently deserted.
ANTIQUE VEHICLE: A motor vehicle that is more than twenty five (25) years of
age or a bona fide replica thereof and which is driven on the highways only
going to and returning from an antique auto show or an exhibition, or for
servicing or demonstration, or a firefighting vehicle more than twenty (20)
years old which is not used as firefighting equipment but is used only for the
purpose of exhibition of demonstration.
HIGHWAY: Any street, alley, or public way within the city. (Ord. 112, 12-28-
1970; amd. 2008 Code)
4-2-2: ABANDONMENT PROHIBITED; REMOVAL AUTHORIZED:
The abandonment of a motor vehicle or other vehicle or any part thereof on any
highway in the city is unlawful and subject to penalties as set forth herein.
The abandonment of a motor vehicle or other vehicle or any part thereof on
private or public property, other than a highway, in view of the general
public, anywhere in the city is unlawful, except on property of the owner or
bailee of such abandoned vehicle. A motor vehicle or other vehicle or any part
thereof so abandoned on private property may be authorized for removal by or
upon the order of the city police department after a waiting period of seven
(7) days or more has expired. (Ord. 112, 12-28-1970)
4-2-3: DUTY TO NOTIFY POLICE OF ABANDONED, UNCLAIMED VEHICLE:
When an abandoned, lost, stolen or unclaimed motor vehicle or other vehicle
comes into the temporary possession or custody of a person in this state not
the owner of the vehicle, such person shall immediately notify the city police
department when the vehicle is within the corporate limits of the city. Upon
receipt of such notification, the police department shall authorize a towing
service to remove and take possession of the abandoned, lost, stolen or
unclaimed motor vehicle or other vehicle. The towing service will safely keep
the towed vehicle and its contents and maintain a record of the tow until the
vehicle is claimed by the owner or any other person legally entitled to
possession thereof, or until it is disposed of as provided in this chapter.
(Ord. 112, 12-28-1970)
4-2-4: ABANDONED, WRECKED VEHICLE ON STREET:
   A.   When a motor vehicle or other vehicle is abandoned on a highway in the
city ten (10) hours or more, its removal by a towing service may be authorized
by order of the city police department.
   B.   When an abandoned, unattended, wrecked, burned or partially dismantled
motor vehicle or other vehicle is creating a traffic hazard because of its
position in relation to the highway or its physical appearance is causing the
impeding of traffic, its immediate removal from the highway by a towing service
may be authorized by order of the city police department.
   C.   When a vehicle removed from either public or private property is
authorized by order of the city police department, the owner of the vehicle
will be responsible for all towing costs. (Ord. 112, 12-28-1970)
4-2-5: RECORD OF TOWED VEHICLES:
When a motor vehicle or other vehicle is authorized to be towed away, the
police department shall keep and maintain a record of the vehicle towed,
listing the color, year of manufacture, manufacturer's trade name,
manufacturer's series name, body style, vehicle identification number and
license plate year and number and registration sticker year and number
displayed on the vehicle. The record shall also include the date and hour of
tow, location towed from, location towed to, reason for towing and the name of
the officer authorizing the tow. (Ord. 112, 12-28-1970; amd. 2008 Code)
4-2-6: OWNER UNKNOWN:
   A.   When the police department does not know the identity of the registered
owner, lien holder or other legally entitled person, it will cause the motor
vehicle registration records of the state of Illinois to be searched by a
directed communication to the secretary of state for the purpose of obtaining
the required ownership information.
   B.   The police department will cause the stolen motor vehicle files of the
Illinois state police to be searched by a directed communication to the
Illinois state police for stolen or wanted information on the vehicle. When the
Illinois state police files are searched with negative results, the information
contained in the national crime information center (NCIC) files will be
searched by the Illinois state police. The information determined from these
record searches will be used by the police department in sending a notification
by certified mail to the registered owner, lien holder or legally entitled
person advising where the vehicle is held, requesting a disposition be made and
setting forth public sale information.
   C.   When the registered owner, lien holder or other person legally entitled
to the possession of a motor vehicle or other vehicle cannot be identified from
the registration files of this state or from the registration files of a
foreign state, if applicable, the police department shall notify the Illinois
state police for the purpose of identifying the vehicle owner or other person
legally entitled to the possession of the vehicle. The information obtained by
the Illinois state police will be immediately forwarded to the police
department for notification of the owner. (Ord. 112, 12-28-1970; amd. 2008
Code)
4-2-7: RECLAMATION OF VEHICLE:
Any time before a motor vehicle or other vehicle is sold at public sale or
disposed of as provided herein, the owner, lien holder or other person legally
entitled to its possession may reclaim the vehicle by presenting to the police
department proof of ownership or proof of the right to possession of the
vehicle. No vehicle shall be released to the owner or other person under this
section until all towing and storage charges have been paid. (Ord. 112, 12-28-
1970; amd. 2008 Code)
4-2-8: SALE AND DISPOSAL OF VEHICLE:
   A.   Vehicles Seven Years Of Age Or Newer:
      1.   Known Owner: Whenever an abandoned, lost, stolen or unclaimed motor
vehicle or other vehicle, seven (7) years of age or newer, remains unclaimed by
the registered owner, lien holder or other legally entitled person for a period
of thirty (30) days after notice has been given as provided herein, the police
department shall cause it to be sold at public sale to the highest bidder.
Notice of time and place of the sale shall be posted in a conspicuous place for
at least ten (10) days prior to the sale on the premises where the vehicle has
been impounded. At least ten (10) days prior to the sale, the police department
shall cause a notice of the time and place of the sale to be sent by certified
mail to the registered owner or other person known by the police department or
towing service to be legally entitled to the possession of the vehicle. Such
notice shall contain a complete description of the vehicle to be sold and what
steps must be taken by any legally entitled person to reclaim the vehicle. In
those instances where the certified notification specified herein has been
returned by the postal authorities to the police department due to the
addressee having moved or being unknown at the address obtained from the
registration records of this state, the sending of a second certified notice
will not be required.
      2.   Unknown Owner: When the identity of the registered owner, lien
holder or other legally entitled persons of an abandoned, lost or unclaimed
vehicle of seven (7) years of age or newer cannot be determined by any means
provided for in this chapter, the vehicle may be sold as provided herein or
disposed of in the manner authorized by this chapter without notice to any
person whose identity cannot be determined.
   B.   Vehicles Older Than Seven Years: When an abandoned vehicle of more than
seven (7) years of age is impounded as specified by this chapter, or when any
such vehicle is towed at the request or with the consent of the owner or
operator and is subsequently abandoned, it will be kept in custody or storage
for a minimum of ten (10) days for the purpose of determining the identity of
the registered owner, lien holder, or other legally entitled persons and
contacting the registered owner, lien holder, or other legally entitled persons
by the U.S. mail, public service or in person for a determination of
disposition and an examination of the state police stolen vehicle files for
theft and wanted information. At the expiration of the ten (10) day period,
without the benefit of disposition information being received from the
registered owner, lien holder, or other legally entitled persons, the vehicle
shall be disposed of as junk or salvage. (Ord. 112, 12-28-1970; amd. 2008 Code)
   C.   Hazardous Dilapidated Vehicles: Any hazardous dilapidated motor vehicle
impounded pursuant to the provisions of this chapter, whether impounded at a
public facility or on the property of private towing service, shall be kept in
custody for a period of ten (10) days for the purpose of determining the
identity of the registered owner or lien holder and contacting such owner or
lien holder, if known, by regular U.S. mail. At the expiration of the ten (10)
day period, without benefit of disposition information being received from the
registered owner or lien holder, the police department will authorize the
disposal of the vehicle as junk. (2008 Code)
   D.   Records Kept: When a motor vehicle or other vehicle in the custody of
the police department is reclaimed by the registered owner or other legally
entitled person, or when the vehicle is sold at public sale or otherwise
disposed of as provided in this chapter, a report of the transaction will be
maintained by the police department for a period of one year from the date of
the sale or disposal.
   E.   Antique Vehicles Exempt: A motor vehicle or other vehicle classified as
an antique vehicle is excluded from this section. (Ord. 112, 12-28-1970)
4-2-9: DISPOSITION OF REVENUE:
When a vehicle located within the corporate limits of the city is authorized to
be towed away by the police and disposed of as set forth in this chapter, the
proceeds of the public sale or disposition after the deduction of towing,
storage and processing charges shall be deposited in the city treasury. (Ord.
112, 12-28-1970)
4-2-10: NONLIABILITY OF POLICE AND TOWING SERVICE:
Any police officer or towing service owner, operator or employee shall not be
held to answer or be liable for damages in any action brought by the registered
owner, former registered owner, or legal representative, or any other person
legally entitled to the possession of a motor vehicle or other vehicle when the
vehicle was processed and sold or disposed of as provided by this chapter.
(Ord. 112, 12-28-1970)
4-2-11: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter, upon conviction, shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each day such violation is committed or permitted to
continue shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable hereunder
as such. (Ord. 112, 12-28-1970; amd. 2008 Code)
CHAPTER 3
BURNING REGULATIONS 1
SECTION:
4-3-1: Trash, Rubbish And Garbage
4-3-2: Landscape Waste
4-3-3: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  4-1E-4 of this title.
4-3-1: TRASH, RUBBISH AND GARBAGE:
   A.   Burning of yard waste, garbage, construction materials, etc. is
prohibited. Fire pits are considered recreational fires. They should be a
sufficient distance from the structure or combustible materials to protect from
wind or other source reaching the structure. For portable outdoor fireplaces,
the standards shall also apply.
   B.   Both types of open burning (for all properties) must meet the several
conditions that follow:
      1.   Must use only dry wood or charcoal fuel;
      2.   Must be kept to a manageable size (three foot (3') diameter or less/
two foot (2') height or less);
      3.   Must have extinguishing capability readily available (garden hose/
fire extinguisher)
      4.   Must be constantly attended until completely extinguished;
      5.   Must be kept between the hours of seven o’clock (7:00) A.M. and
eleven o’clock (11:00) P.M.;
      6.   Burning is not allowed during high winds (in excess of twenty (20)
mph);
      7.   Burning is not allowed during times of high fire;
      8.   There is no imminent health hazard to persons in the area. (Ord.
257, 3-26-1990; Ord. 443, 9-22-2020)
4-3-2: LANDSCAPE WASTE:
The burning of "landscape waste", as that term is defined in section 3.270 of
the Illinois environmental protection act 1 , is prohibited. (Ord. 257, 3-26-
1990; amd. 2008 Code)
 
Notes
1 2. 415 ILCS 5/3.270.
4-3-3: PENALTY:
Any violation of any provision of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. The continued burning of any item prohibited in this
chapter shall constitute and be punishable as a separate offense. (Ord. 257, 3-
26-1990; amd. 2008 Code)
CHAPTER 4
CURBSIDE RECYCLING PROGRAM
SECTION:
4-4-1: Program Created
4-4-2: Supervision
4-4-3: Definition
4-4-4: Use Of Bins Or Bags
4-4-5: Pick Up Of Recyclables
4-4-6: Voluntary Participation In Program
4-4-7: Violations; Penalties
4-4-1: PROGRAM CREATED:
A curbside recycling program is hereby created in the city. The program shall
begin on or after January 1, 1993. The program shall allow for the pick up of
recyclable materials by one or more waste haulers. (Ord. 283, 10-18-1993)
4-4-2: SUPERVISION:
The curbside recycling program shall be supervised by the individual appointed
by the mayor. That person shall be the city recycling coordinator and is
empowered to make rules, consistent with this chapter, for the orderly, safe
and sanitary operation of the program. Such rules and any amendments shall be
published in pamphlet form from time to time. (Ord. 283, 10-18-1993; amd. 2008
Code)
4-4-3: DEFINITION:
"Recyclable materials" include, but are not limited to, old newspaper, soft
drink containers made from high density polyethylene (HDPE), milk jugs made
from polyethylene terephthalate (PETE), bimetal food and beverage cans,
aluminum, clear glass, brown glass and green glass. (Ord. 283, 10-18-1993)
4-4-4: USE OF BINS OR BAGS:
All recyclable materials shall be placed in bins or kraft paper bags. (Ord.
283, 10-18-1993)
4-4-5: PICK UP OF RECYCLABLES:
All recyclable materials shall be picked up at curbside or, if a resident has
paid the waste hauler for special service, at another location on the
resident's premises. (Ord. 283, 10-18-1993)
4-4-6: VOLUNTARY PARTICIPATION IN PROGRAM:
Participation by residents shall be promoted by free distribution of one
recycling bin to each residence. However, participation by residents shall be
voluntary, not mandatory. (Ord. 283, 10-18-1993)
4-4-7: VIOLATIONS; PENALTIES:
   A.   Violations:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to set out recyclable materials
for collection more than twenty four (24) hours before the expected time of
collection.
      2.   It shall be unlawful for any person, other than the resident or an
employee of a waste hauler, to remove recyclable materials from that resident's
recycling bin or other recycling container. (Ord. 283, 10-18-1993)
   B.   Penalties: A first offense shall be punished only by issuance of a
written warning. Any second or subsequent violation of subsection A1 or A2 of
this section shall be punishable by a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each violation shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord.
283, 10-18-1993; amd. 2008 Code)
CHAPTER 5
TREE PRESERVATION
SECTION:
4-5-1: Title
4-5-2: Purpose And Intent
4-5-3: Definitions
4-5-4: Trimming And Removal Of Protected Trees
4-5-5: Public Nuisance Trees
4-5-6: Responsibility Of Owners And Occupants
4-5-7: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
4-5-8: Arborist Registration
4-5-9: Administration And Enforcement Officials
4-5-10: Notice Of Provisions
4-5-11: Appeals
4-5-12: Unauthorized Entry Onto Private Property
4-5-13: Penalty
4-5-1: TITLE:
This chapter may be cited as the LELAND GROVE TREE PRESERVATION ORDINANCE.
(Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
4-5-2: PURPOSE AND INTENT:
   A.   The city council finds that the preservation of existing trees and the
promotion of new planting is a public purpose that protects the public health,
safety, and welfare and the environment and aesthetics of the city and its
citizens.
   B.   The urban forest serves a wide variety of functions that promote the
purposes of this chapter, as follows:
      1.   Ensuring that trimming and removal of trees is carried out in a
responsible and safe manner.
      2.   Enhancing visual and aesthetic qualities of the city.
      3.   Creating a civic identity for the citizens of the city of Leland
Grove, a city named for its trees.
   C.   It is the intention of the city council that this chapter be enforced
so as to promote its purposes while simultaneously recognizing the legitimate
interests of owners of private property. (Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
4-5-3: DEFINITIONS:
In this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings ascribed
to them in this section:
ARBORIST: A person who, for profit:
   A.   Diagnoses the condition of trees and recommends or supervises their
treatment; or
   B.   In any manner treats trees by feeding, fertilizing, pruning, trimming,
removing, bracing, treating cavities, or other methods.
CITY: The city of Leland Grove, Illinois.
OVERHEAD TRANSMISSION LINES: The lines of a public utility that are suspended
aboveground and that have a sag or sway within ten feet (10') of the air space
occupied by a tree.
PERSON: Includes any individual, corporation, partnership, association, or
other legal entity.
PROTECTED TREE: A tree whose trunk enters the ground within a public easement
area or road right of way. A volunteer seedling less than two feet (2') tall is
not a protected tree.
PUBLIC EASEMENT AREA: A road right of way or other easement upon which the
public has a right of passage.
PUBLIC NUISANCE TREE: A tree determined by the city council to be a public
nuisance.
ROAD RIGHT OF WAY: The entire area, whether or not owned by the city, that is
dedicated to the purpose of public roads and upon which the city maintains a
roadway.
SAG AND SWAY: The distance determined by the city administrator that overhead
public utility transmission lines will move vertically and horizontally at
midspan due to normal and customary weather conditions. (Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
4-5-4: TRIMMING AND REMOVAL OF PROTECTED TREES:
   A.   Approval Required: A protected tree may be trimmed or removed only with
the approval of and within the limits set by the city administrator. If the
trimming or removal: 1) does not impair the public health, safety, welfare, or
environment; 2) does not unreasonably impair the value of adjoining property;
3) is a reasonable solution to the stated necessity for the trimming or
removal; and 4) is consistent with the overall purposes of this chapter, then
the city administrator shall grant approval, subject to reasonable limitations
and requirements set by the city administrator.
   B.   Notice To Adjacent Property Owners: After having received the approval
of the city administrator, the person with approval to trim or remove a
protected tree must give written notice to the owner or occupant of each parcel
of property located in whole or in part within twenty feet (20') of the trunk
of the tree to be trimmed or removed. The notice must indicate whether the tree
is to be trimmed or removed, and must indicate the time frame in which the
trimming or removal will begin, which must be at least seven (7) calendar days
after the notice has been delivered to the last of each of those entitled to
notice.
   C.   Trimming Standards And Guidelines: Unless the city administrator, with
the approval of the city council, provides otherwise, all trimming of protected
trees shall be done based on the standards and guidelines set forth in the most
current edition of: 1) "Pruning Trees Near Electric Utility Lines" by Dr. Alex
Shigo; 2) the National Arborist Association in "Pruning Standards For Shade
Trees"; and 3) "American National Standards For Tree Care Operations - Tree,
Shrub And Other Woody Plant Maintenance - Standard Practices", published by the
American National Standards Institute, Inc.
   D.   Electric Line Clearance Standards:
      1.   No person may trim a tree within ten feet (10') of an overhead
transmission line unless that person has a utility line arborist certification
in accordance with OHSA 1910269.
      2.   Protected trees may need to be trimmed to clearances in excess of
accepted standards for aesthetic or safety reasons. In that case, the city
administrator may issue a permit allowing a deviation from those clearance
standards to the extent and in the manner set forth in the permit. No fee shall
be charged for that permit. No tree trimming shall be done by any person, as
set forth in this subsection D2, except as authorized by the city
administrator.
      3.   Nothing in this chapter shall be interpreted as preventing any
person from trimming or removing a tree or portion of a tree for the purpose of
restoring electric power that has been interrupted by reason of that tree or
portion of it having come into contact with an overhead transmission line.
   E.   Replacement Of Removed Trees: The standards and guidelines for trimming
and removal are those set forth in subsection C of this section.
      1.   If a protected tree is removed, either with or without the approval
of the city administrator, then the person who removed the tree, at his or her
cost, must promptly replace it with a tree or shrub approved by the city
administrator. For good cause shown, the city council may waive the requirement
of replacing the tree.
      2.   If, without the approval of the city administrator, a protected tree
is removed or is significantly damaged, whether by excessive trimming or
otherwise, then the person who removed or damaged the tree, at his or her cost,
must promptly replace the tree as provided in subsection E1 of this section
and, in addition, must pay a penalty to the city as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
4-5-5: PUBLIC NUISANCE TREES:
   A.   The city council may specify trees that are considered to be a public
nuisance.
      1.   Trees designated to be a public nuisance may not be planted either
on public right of way or on private property.
      2.   Trees designated to be a public nuisance are not protected trees as
defined in this chapter and may be removed from the public right of way by the
owner(s) of adjacent property(ies) if said owner(s) is willing to bear the cost
of removal.
      3.   A no cost permit must be obtained from the city administrator before
a nuisance tree is removed from any city right of way. As part of the permit
process, the city administrator will discuss with the applicant what trees are
approved for replacement and other requirements such as minimum height of the
replacement. The kind of replacement tree and any such requirements shall be
listed on the permit. A waiver for cause may be requested from and may be
granted by the city administrator.
   B.   Trees declared to be a public nuisance:
      1.   Sweet gum. (Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
4-5-6: RESPONSIBILITY OF OWNERS AND OCCUPANTS:
   A.   The owner of the property where a tree is located, and the occupant of
that property if it is not owner occupied, must keep the tree trimmed: 1) so as
not to impede the passage of persons or vehicles along public easement areas;
2) so as not to obstruct the reflection of streetlights; 3) so as not to hide
from view or obstruct all or any part of a traffic control device or street
identification sign; and 4) so as not to threaten the safety of persons or
property.
   B.   If an owner or occupant is in violation of subsection A of this
section, it is the duty of the city administrator to notify that owner or
occupant in writing that, within five (5) calendar days after delivery of the
notice, the owner or occupant must trim the tree. The notice requirement under
subsection
4-5-4B of this chapter does not apply to this situation. If the owner or
occupant is notified and neglects or refuses to comply with this section, then
the owner or occupant is in violation of this chapter, and the city
administrator may cause the tree to be trimmed at the cost to that owner or
occupant. If a violation of subsection A of this section causes an imminent
danger to persons or property, then the city administrator may cause the
violation to be corrected and may charge the cost to the owner or occupant.
Costs charged to the owner or occupant are a lien on the premises. The lien may
be enforced as provided by law. (Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
4-5-7: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Enumeration Of Prohibited Acts And Conditions: Each of the following is
a violation of this chapter:
      1.   To plant or cause to be planted a tree that is on the list of
prohibited trees established and modified from time to time by the city
administrator if that tree, if planted, would be a protected tree.
      2.   To plant or cause to be planted a tree that has been declared a
public nuisance by the city council, whether planted on a public right of way
or on private property.
      3.   To plant or cause to be planted any tree in a public easement area
unless approved in writing by the city administrator. In granting or denying
approval, the city administrator shall take into consideration the distance
from the roadway, the expected height and overhang of the tree at maturity, and
any potential interference with preexisting overhead transmission lines.
      4.   To deposit, store, or maintain any stone, brick, sand, concrete, or
other material that may reasonably be expected to impede the free passage of
water, air, or fertilizer to the roots of any protected tree.
      5.   To cause or allow any gaseous, liquid, or solid substance that
reasonably may be expected to be toxic or otherwise harmful to trees to be
located where that substance reasonably may be expected to affect a protected
tree.
      6.   To attach any sign, advertisement, or notice to any protected tree.
      7.   To attach any line, wire, or rope to any protected tree without the
permission of the city administrator. Any person, including a public utility,
that maintains poles, lines, wires, or ropes must, absent a specific and
contrary provision in a franchise or other agreement with the city: a) keep
those poles, lines, wires, or ropes free from and as far away as possible from
protected trees; and b) keep protected trees near any pole, line, wire, or rope
properly trimmed, subject to the supervision of the city administrator, so that
no injury will be done either to the poles, lines, wires, or ropes or to the
trees.
      8.   For any person maintaining a gas pipe to fail to keep that pipe free
from leaks so that no injury is done to any protected tree.
      9.   For any person to make an excavation and fail to take proper care to
avoid injury to the roots of any protected tree. Whenever possible, tunneling
must be used instead of trenching.
   B.   Notice Of Violations; City Action; Costs: The city administrator may
order any person who violates any provision of this section to correct the
violation by giving written notice to that person. If that person fails to
correct the violation within a reasonable time after the notice, the City
Administrator may correct the violation, and that person shall be charged with
the expenses of correcting the violation. Those expenses may be collected by
the City through any available legal means, including an action commenced in
the Circuit Court. (Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
4-5-8: ARBORIST REGISTRATION:
   A.   Registration Required; Term; No Fee: Each arborist must register with
the City Administrator before doing business within the City. A registration is
valid for one (1) year from the date of issuance. No fee is required for the
registration.
   B.   Exemption From Registration: Any person acting within the scope of his
or her employment with a public utility or with the City is exempt from
registration.
   C.   Violations; Penalty: A person who violates this section is subject to
the penalty under section
4-5-13 of this chapter for each violation. A violation with respect to any
single tree constitutes a separate violation. For example, an arborist who
trims two (2) trees without having registered commits two (2) separate
violations. (Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
4-5-9: ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT OFFICIALS:
   A.   In administering this chapter, the City Administrator may consult with
any person who, by education, training, and experience, has significant
expertise in the respective trades.
   B.   Except as otherwise provided in the Intergovernmental Agreement with
Sangamon County, the City Police Department, and the City Administrator each
have the authority to enforce this chapter. (Ord. 417, 3-28-2017)
4-5-10: NOTICE OF PROVISIONS:
The City Administrator shall, from time to time, take reasonable steps to
ensure that all of the citizens and property owners of the City and all
registered arborists are informed as to the provisions of this chapter and any
lists maintained by the City Administrator pursuant to this chapter. When a
person applies for a building and zoning permit or for registration as an
arborist, the City Administrator must provide this chapter and any lists to the
applicant. (Ord. 417, 3-28-2017)
4-5-11: APPEALS:
A petitioner who is aggrieved by any decision of the City Administrator under
this chapter may appeal that decision to the City Council by filing a notice of
appeal with the City Clerk no later than thirty (30) days after the person is
notified of the decision. The Mayor shall set a time for hearing the appeal,
which may be heard at either a regular or special meeting of the City Council.
Due and reasonable notice of the hearing shall be given to the person making
the appeal and, as appropriate, to nearby property owners. The person making
the appeal, who may be represented by an attorney, and the City Administrator
shall each be given the opportunity to present testimony and other evidence to
the City Council. (Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
4-5-12: UNAUTHORIZED ENTRY ONTO PRIVATE PROPERTY:
Except for officers, employees, and agents of the City, nothing in this chapter
shall be construed to authorize any person to enter upon private property,
including, without limitation: a) any utility easement area; or b) any portion
of a road right-of- way that is clearly not intended to be open to vehicular or
pedestrian traffic. Nothing in this chapter, however, is intended to prohibit
any person from entering onto private property if that person has an
independent right to do so. (Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
4-5-13: PENALTY:
In addition to all other penalties or assessments under this chapter or
otherwise provided by law, a person who violates any provision of this chapter
is subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code for each violation. The City Administrator shall assess the
penalty after taking the nature and relevant circumstances of the violation
into consideration. (Ord. 378, 5-22-2012)
CHAPTER 6
SEPTIC TANKS
SECTION:
4-6-1: Septic Tanks For Dwellings Prohibited
4-6-1: SEPTIC TANKS FOR DWELLINGS PROHIBITED:
No dwelling structure shall hereafter be constructed or remodeled in the city
unless provision is made to construct the sewer drain from the property to a
sanitary sewer maintained by the Springfield sanitary district. It shall be
illegal to use a septic tank or private sewage treatment system in the city to
dispose of sewage from any dwelling structure hereafter constructed or
remodeled in the city. (Ord. 210, 3-25-1985)
CHAPTER 7
VACANT PROPERTY REGISTRATION AND CARE
SECTION:
4-7-1: Definitions
4-7-2: Registration
4-7-3: Maintenance And Upkeep
4-7-4: Penalty
4-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
VACANT PROPERTY: A residential property in which no one is residing on a
permanent basis. Visitation on a sporadic basis to the property by an owner or
their designee does not qualify as residence within the property. (Ord. 422, 2-
27-2018)
4-7-2: REGISTRATION:
At the conclusion of thirty (30) days with no resident in the property, it is
required of all owners of property to register the fact that the property is
vacant. Such registration shall be on forms prepared and maintained at the
offices of the City. (Ord. 422, 2-27-2018)
4-7-3: MAINTENANCE AND UPKEEP:
Owners of property which are vacant in addition to registration with the City,
must maintain the property in a safe manner. All entrances or windows must be
locked or permanently affixed to prohibit access by unauthorized individuals.
