Repairs necessary to maintain the safety of the home must be made within a
timely manner. Vegetation and other plant material must be periodically cut and
removed in a manner consistent with a residential neighborhood in the City of
Leland Grove. (Ord. 422, 2-27-2018)
4-7-4: PENALTY:
Violation of any provision of this chapter shall be considered a Class C
violation in accordance with section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 422, 2-27-2018)
TITLE 5
POLICE AND PUBLIC SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
DOGS AND CATS
SECTION:
5-1-1: Definition
5-1-2: Running At Large Prohibited
5-1-3: Nuisance Dogs And Cats
5-1-4: Impoundment And Redemption Provisions
5-1-5: Penalty
5-1-1: DEFINITION:
The term "animal control officer", as used in this chapter, includes a Sangamon
County animal control officer whose services are obtained through an
intergovernmental contract. (Ord. 297, 4-25-1995)
5-1-2: RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
No dog or cat shall be permitted by the owner or keeper thereof to run at large
within the city. (Ord. 297, 4-25-1995)
5-1-3: NUISANCE DOGS AND CATS 1 :
Any dog or cat which may in any manner disturb the peace and quiet of any
person or neighborhood, or shall destroy or in any manner injure any person,
animal, plant, shrub or other property not on the premises of its owner or
keeper, is hereby declared to be a public nuisance, and such dog or cat shall
be taken up and impounded. (Ord. 297, 4-25-1995)
 
Notes
1 1. See section 4-1B-4 of this code for feces accumulation prohibitions.
5-1-4: IMPOUNDMENT AND REDEMPTION PROVISIONS:
   A.   Impoundment Authorized: It shall be the duty of the animal control
officer to catch, take up, and impound at the county animal shelter any dog or
cat found running at large in the city contrary to the provisions of this
chapter.
   B.   Notice Of Impoundment: If ownership of the dog or cat can be
established through reasonable effort, the owner or keeper of such dog or cat
shall be given notice by mail of such impounding.
   C.   Use Of County Animal Shelter: Any dog or cat taken up or caught by the
animal control officer shall be impounded at the county animal shelter, and
shall be held at the county animal shelter pursuant to the regulations
established by the county.
   D.   Redemption Of Impounded Dog Or Cat: Any owner or keeper desiring to
redeem an impounded dog or cat which was caught and impounded by the animal
control officer shall first pay a fee of five dollars ($5.00) to the city clerk
or the city police department and obtain a receipt for such payment, which
shall be presented to the officials at the county animal shelter. The owner or
keeper may then redeem the impounded dog or cat by paying such other charges as
may be imposed by the county animal shelter as provided by law.
   E.   Disposition Of Unredeemed Dogs And Cats: Any dog or cat not redeemed by
its owner or keeper shall be disposed of as provided by regulations established
by the county. (Ord. 297, 4-25-1995)
5-1-5: PENALTY:
In addition to impoundment of a dog or cat, any owner or keeper of a dog or cat
who violates the provisions of this chapter by allowing a dog or cat to run at
large or by allowing such animal to behave as a public nuisance may be
prosecuted. Upon conviction, each offense shall be punished by a fine as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each day that any violation of this chapter shall occur or
continue shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 297, 4-25-1995; amd. 2008
Code)
CHAPTER 2
FIRE PREVENTION AND CONTROL
SECTION:
5-2-1: Fire Hazards; Storage Of Certain Materials Prohibited
5-2-2: Fireworks
5-2-1: FIRE HAZARDS; STORAGE OF CERTAIN MATERIALS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Prohibited Materials: It is hereby declared to be a nuisance for any
person to store in any building in the city, other than a one- or two-family
dwelling house occupied by an owner or tenant, any of the following materials
or items:
      1.   Ten (10) or more mattresses.
      2.   Rugs and carpeting material in excess of the quantity required to
carpet the floors in a one- or two-family dwelling house.
      3.   Welding gases, paint, oil, and other petroleum products in excess of
five (5) gallons.
      4.   Furniture consisting of tables, chairs, and beds in excess of the
quantity required to furnish a one- or two-family dwelling house.
      5.   Lumber.
      6.   Other combustible materials.
   B.   Removal Required; Notice: Any person found to be in violation of this
section shall remove the combustible materials within thirty (30) days after
notice is sent by the city by certified mail. (Ord. 244, 9-1-1988)
   C.   Penalties: Any person who shall violate, neglect or refuse to comply
with, or who shall maintain or use any building or premises in the city in
violation of any of the provisions of this section shall, upon conviction, be
punished by a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense, and each day that a violation is permitted
or continues to exist shall constitute a separate offense, and in addition to
the above penalty, such actions at law or in equity may be maintained by the
city or any interested persons as may be authorized by law. (Ord. 244, 9-1-
1988; amd. 2008 Code)
5-2-2: FIREWORKS:
   A.   Definition: As used in this section, the term "fireworks" means and
includes any explosive composition, or any substance or combination of
substances, or article prepared for the purpose of producing a visible or
audible effect of a temporary exhibitional nature by explosion, combustion,
deflagration or detonation, and shall include blank cartridges, toy cannons in
which explosives are used, the type of balloons which require fire underneath
to propel the same, firecrackers, torpedoes, sky rockets, Roman candles, bombs
or other fireworks of like construction and any fireworks containing any
explosive compound, or any tablets or other device containing any explosive
substance or containing combustible substances producing visual effects, or any
other substance which is regulated by Illinois law, including 425 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 30/1 through 35/5; provided, however, that the term
"fireworks" shall not include snake or glowworm pellets; smoke devices; trick
noisemakers known as "party poppers", "booby traps", "snappers", "trick
matches", "cigarette loads", and "auto burglar alarms"; sparklers, toy pistols,
toy canes, toy guns, or other devices in which paper or plastic caps containing
0.25 grains or less of explosive compound are used, provided they are so
constructed that the hand cannot come in contact with the cap when in place for
the explosion, and toy pistol paper or plastic caps which contain less than
0.25 grains of explosive mixture. The use of such excluded articles shall be
permitted at all times. (Ord. 334, 8-26-2003; amd. 2008 Code)
   B.   Manufacture Of Fireworks: The manufacture of fireworks within the city
limits is prohibited except as authorized under the laws of the state, 425
Illinois Compiled Statutes 30/1 through 35/5 (or other applicable state law).
   C.   Sale Of Fireworks: No person shall offer for sale, expose for sale, or
sell at retail any fireworks within the city limits.
   D.   Display Of Fireworks; Permit Requirements:
      1.   Permit Required: No person shall possess, store, use, or explode any
fireworks unless he shall have been issued a fireworks display permit. No
person shall sell or use or explode any fireworks within the city without first
obtaining a permit as provided herein.
      2.   Eligibility For Permit:
         a.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) years shall be
eligible to be issued a display permit.
         b.   The city clerk is authorized to grant permits to groups of three
(3) or more adult individuals for supervised public displays of fireworks in
the city in accordance with the provisions of 425 Illinois Compiled Statutes
35/2.
      3.   Application For Permit: Any group of three (3) or more adult
individuals desiring a permit for a supervised public display of fireworks
shall file a written application with the city clerk at least fifteen (15) days
prior to the date of the display. Applications for such fireworks displays
shall state the names, addresses and ages of the three (3) or more adult
individuals applying for such permit; the date of the display; the location of
the display; and the location where the fireworks will be stored prior to the
display.
      4.   Bond: Each person shall furnish an indemnity bond in a sum of not
less than one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) conditioned on the compliance with
the provisions of this section.
      5.   Permit Fee: The city clerk shall collect a fee of ten dollars
($10.00) for the issuance of any permit authorized by this section.
      6.   Investigation Of Applicant; Approval Or Denial Of Permit: Each
application shall be investigated to determine whether the display is of a
character and so located so as not to constitute an unreasonable hazard to any
person or property. If, upon completion of the investigation, it is determined
that all requirements of this section are satisfied, the permit shall be
approved and issued. A copy of each permit shall be forwarded by the office of
the city clerk to the chief of police not less than forty eight (48) hours
before the display. In the event that the application is not approved, the
applicant shall be informed in writing of the reasons therefor.
      7.   Nontransferability Of Permit: No permit granted hereunder shall be
transferable. Only the person named on the permit shall be authorized to
possess and display fireworks.
      8.   Conditions Of Permit:
         a.   Supervised public displays of fireworks shall be of such a
character, and so located, discharged or fired, so as not to be hazardous to
property or endanger any person.
         b.   The possession and use of fireworks by the permittee shall be
lawful only for the purpose of display contained in the permit.
         c.   Displays shall not be conducted before ten o'clock (10:00) A.M.
or after ten thirty o'clock (10:30) P.M., except where prior approval is
granted for special programs.
   E.   Responsibility Of Parent Or Guardian: It shall be the responsibility of
parents or legal guardians of unemancipated persons under the age of eighteen
(18) years to assure that those persons comply with the restrictions of this
section. No parent or legal guardian of those persons shall knowingly permit or
assist in the violation of this section by any unemancipated person under the
age of eighteen (18) years.
   F.   Exemptions From Provisions: Nothing in this section shall be construed
to prohibit the use of fireworks by railroads or other transportation agencies
for signal purposes or illumination, or the sale or use of blank cartridges for
a show or theater, or for ceremonial purposes in athletics or sports, or for
use by military forces of the state of Illinois, the United States, or
authorized emergency services agencies such as rescue squad or fire and police
departments of the city or other municipalities. (Ord. 334, 8-26-2003)
CHAPTER 3
WEAPONS
SECTION:
5-3-1: Firearms
5-3-1: FIREARMS:
   A.   Discharge Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person to fire or
discharge any rifle, shotgun, pistol, revolver or other firearm, or air rifle
or air pistol, within the city; provided, however, that this subsection shall
not apply to police officers in the performance of their lawful duties. (Ord.
79, 5-18-1964)
   B.   Responsibility Of Parent Or Guardian: It shall be unlawful for any
parent or guardian of any person under eighteen (18) years of age to permit or
allow such person under eighteen (18) years of age to handle or have in his
possession within the city any rifle, shotgun, pistol or revolver or other
firearm, or any air rifle or air pistol, or any other similar weapon, which, if
discharged, is of sufficient force or power to inflict bodily injury.
   C.   Penalty: Any person found guilty of violating any provision of this
section shall be punished by a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 79, 5-18-1964; amd. 2008 Code)
CHAPTER 3.1
CANNABIS AND RELATED MATERIALS
SECTION:
5-3.1-1: Possession Of Cannabis Or The Synthetic Form Commonly Known As K2
Prohibited
5-3.1-2: Possession Of Drug Paraphernalia Prohibited
5-3.1-3: Tobacco And Minors
5-3.1-4: Penalty
5-3.1-1: POSSESSION OF CANNABIS OR THE SYNTHETIC FORM COMMONLY KNOWN AS K2
PROHIBITED:
   A.   No person shall possess ten grams (10 g) or less of any substance
containing cannabis, or the synthetic form of cannabis, 1-pentyl-3-(1-napthoyl)
indole, commonly known as K2.
   B.   For the purpose of this section, cannabis includes marijuana, hashish
and other substances which are identified as including any parts of the plant
cannabis sativa, whether growing or not; the seeds thereof, the resin extracted
from any part of such plant; and any compound, manufacture, salt, derivative,
and all other cannabinol derivatives, including its naturally occurring or
synthetically produced ingredients, whether produced directly or indirectly by
extraction, or independently by means of chemical synthesis or by a combination
of extraction and chemical synthesis; but shall not include the mature stalks
of such plant, fiber produced from such stalks, oil or cake made from the seeds
of such plant, any other compound, manufacture, salt, derivative, mixture or
preparation of such mature stalks (except the resin extracted therefrom),
fiber, oil or cake, or the sterilized seed of such plant which is incapable of
germinating. (Ord. 416, 10-25-2016)
5-3.1-2: POSSESSION OF DRUG PARAPHERNALIA PROHIBITED:
   A.   No person shall knowingly possess any item of drug paraphernalia with
the intent to use it for the purpose of unlawfully ingesting, inhaling or
otherwise introducing cannabis or a controlled substance into the human body.
   B.   As used in this section, the following terms shall include and have the
following meanings:
    CANNABIS: Any substance defined as cannabis in section 3 of the Illinois
Cannabis Control Act, 720 Illinois Compiled Statutes 550/3 as now or hereafter
amended.
   DRUG PARAPHERNALIA: Any object or device used, designed for use or intended
for use in unlawfully ingesting, smoking, administering, or storing cannabis.
For the purposes of this section, drug paraphernalia includes but is not
limited to:
      1.   Metal, wooden, plastic, glass, stone or ceramic pipes, with or
without screens;
      2.   Water pipes;
      3.   Carburetion tubes and devices;
      4.   Smoking and carburetion masks;
      5.   Roach clips;
      6.   Bongs;
      7.   One-hitters.
(Ord. 416, 10-25-2016)
5-3.1-3: TOBACCO AND MINORS:
   A.   No person shall sell, buy for, distribute samples of or furnish any
cigar, cigarette, smokeless tobacco or tobacco in any of its forms, to any
minor under eighteen (18) years of age.
   B.   No minor under eighteen (18) years of age shall possess, purchase or
attempt to purchase any cigar, cigarette, smokeless tobacco or tobacco in any
of its forms.
   C.   For the purpose of this section, "smokeless tobacco" means any tobacco
products that are suitable for dipping or chewing. (Ord. 416, 10-25-2016)
5-3.1-4: PENALTY:
Whoever commits an offense set forth in this chapter or commits any other act
prohibited thereby for which another penalty is not specifically provided shall
be fined not less than twenty five dollars ($25.00) nor more than five hundred
dollars ($500.00). Whoever commits an offense as set forth in section 131.01(g)
of this chapter shall be fined not less than two hundred dollars ($200.00) nor
more than five hundred dollars ($500.00). Whoever commits an offense as set
forth in section 131.05 of this chapter shall be fined not less than fifty
dollars ($50.00) nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00). Whoever commits
an offense as set forth in sections 131.07, 131.08 and 131.09(b) of this
chapter shall be fined not less than three hundred dollars ($300.00). Whoever
commits an offense as set forth in section 131.09(a) of this chapter shall be
fined not less than five hundred dollars ($500.00). Any person who shall
violate section 131.02 or 131.09 shall, on conviction thereof, be punished by a
fine which may be reduced by no more than twenty five percent (25%) by approved
public or community service of not less than eight (8) hours nor more than
forty (40) hours for each violation. Any person who shall violate section
131.09 shall, on conviction thereof, be punished by a fine and attendance at an
approved course or counseling on the dangers of smoking. (Ord. 416, 10-25-2016)
CHAPTER 4
UNFAIR REAL ESTATE PRACTICES
SECTION:
5-4-1: Declaration Of Policy
5-4-2: Definitions
5-4-3: Prohibited Acts
5-4-4: Limitations
5-4-5: Fair Housing Commission
5-4-6: Grievance Procedure
5-4-7: Sanctions For Violations
5-4-8: Other Proceedings
5-4-9: Penalty
5-4-1: DECLARATION OF POLICY:
It is hereby declared by the city council to be in the best interest of the
health, safety and welfare of the people of the city to assure equal
opportunity to all persons who engage in real estate transactions regardless of
race, color, religion, sex, national origin, ancestry, age, marital status,
physical or mental handicap, military status, sexual orientation, unfavorable
discharge from military service or familial status and, to that end, to
prohibit discrimination in real estate transactions. (Ord. 96, 6-24-1968; amd.
2008 Code)
5-4-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise requires, the following
words and terms shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section:
DISCRIMINATION: Any act by any person who engages in real estate transactions,
which act does not assure equal opportunity to all other persons regardless of
race, color, religion, sex, national origin, ancestry, age, marital status,
physical or mental handicap, military status, sexual orientation, unfavorable
discharge from military service or familial status.
REAL ESTATE: Includes any lot, building, structure or portion thereof in the
city of Leland Grove which is used or occupied, or is maintained, arranged or
designed to be used or occupied, as a home, residence, sleeping place of one or
more persons, place of business or office, but such term shall not include
rooms for rental to one or two (2) persons in a single-family dwelling, the
remainder of which is occupied by: a) the owner or members of his immediate
family; or b) a lessee of the entire dwelling or members of his immediate
family.
REAL ESTATE BROKER: Any natural person, partnership, association or
corporation, or agent thereof, who, for a fee or other valuable consideration,
sells, purchases, exchanges, rents (or offers or negotiates to do any of the
foregoing) real property of another, or holds himself out as engaged in the
business of doing any of the foregoing, or manages and collects rent from the
real property of another. (Ord. 96, 6-24-1968; amd. 2008 Code)
5-4-3: PROHIBITED ACTS:
No owner of real estate, lessee, sublessee, real estate broker or salesperson,
lender, financial institution, advertiser, building contractor or agent of any
of the foregoing shall discriminate against any other person because of the
race, color, religion, sex, national origin, ancestry, age, marital status,
physical or mental handicap, military status, sexual orientation, unfavorable
discharge from military service or familial status of such other person, in
regard to the sale or rental of, or dealings concerning real estate. Any such
discrimination shall be considered an unfair real estate practice. Without
limiting the foregoing, it shall also be an unfair real estate practice and
unlawful for any real estate broker or other person to:
   A.   Publish, circulate, issue or display, or cause to be published,
circulated, issued or displayed, any communication, notice, advertisement,
sign, or other writing of any kind relating to the sale, rental or leasing of
any real estate which will indicate or express any such discrimination.
   B.   Exploit or overcharge any person for real estate because of race,
color, religion, sex, national origin, ancestry, age, marital status, physical
or mental handicap, military status, sexual orientation, unfavorable discharge
from military service or familial status.
   C.   Solicit for sale, lease, or listing for sale or lease, of any real
estate on the grounds of loss of value due to the present or prospective entry
into any neighborhood of any person or persons of any particular race, color,
religion, sex, national origin, ancestry, age, marital status, physical or
mental handicap, military status, sexual orientation, unfavorable discharge
from military service or familial status.
   D.   Make, distribute, or cause to be made or distributed, any written
material or statements designed to induce any owner of real estate to sell or
lease his property because of any present or prospective change in the race,
color, religion, sex, national origin, ancestry, age, marital status, physical
or mental handicap, military status, sexual orientation, unfavorable discharge
from military service or familial status of persons in the neighborhood.
   E.   Refuse to sell, lease or rent any real estate because of the race,
color, religion, sex, national origin, ancestry, age, marital status, physical
or mental handicap, military status, sexual orientation, unfavorable discharge
from military service or familial status of the proposed buyer or tenant.
   F.   Refuse examination of the copies of any listing of real estate by the
fair housing commission created by the provisions of this chapter.
   G.   Enter into a listing agreement which prohibits the sale or rental of
real estate to any person because of race, color, religion, sex, national
origin, ancestry, age, marital status, physical or mental handicap, military
status, sexual orientation, unfavorable discharge from military service or
familial status.
   H.   Act or undertake to act with respect to any real estate, the
disposition of which is prohibited to any person because of race, color,
religion, sex, national origin, ancestry, age, marital status, physical or
mental handicap, military status, sexual orientation, unfavorable discharge
from military service or familial status. (Ord. 96, 6-24-1968; amd. 2008 Code)
5-4-4: LIMITATIONS:
   A.   Nothing in this chapter shall require an owner to offer property to the
public at large before selling or renting it, nor shall this chapter be deemed
to prohibit owners from giving preference to prospective tenants or buyers for
any reason other than race, color, religion, sex, national origin, ancestry,
age, marital status, physical or mental handicap, military status, sexual
orientation, unfavorable discharge from military service or familial status.
(Ord. 96, 6-24-1968; amd. 2008 Code)
   B.   Nothing in this chapter shall require an owner to offer property for
sale or lease to any person if the owner has any reason to believe that such
person is not negotiating for the purchase or lease of such property in good
faith. (Ord. 96, 6-24-1968)
5-4-5: FAIR HOUSING COMMISSION:
   A.   Created; Members; Appointment; Terms; Vacancies: A fair housing
commission shall be established in the following manner:
      1.   There is created by this chapter the fair housing commission,
hereinafter referred to as "the commission", to consist of seven (7) members,
all of whom shall have been bona fide residents of the city for two (2) years
immediately preceding said appointment. The members of the commission shall be
appointed by the mayor, with the advice and consent of the city council.
      2.   The members of the commission shall be appointed for a term of three
(3) years, and in the event any member shall be, or shall during his term
become, unable or unwilling for any reason to serve as a member of the
commission, the mayor shall fill such vacancy by appointment, with the advice
and consent of the city council, for the remainder of the term vacated. All
appointments shall be in writing and shall be filed with the city clerk as a
public record. Upon the initial creation of the commission, two (2) members of
the commission shall be appointed for a term of three (3) years, two (2)
members of the commission for a term of two (2) years and three (3) members for
a term of one year. Thereafter, upon expiration of said terms, the succeeding
member shall be appointed for a term of three (3) years.
      3.   At the first meeting of the commission, subsequent to May 1 of each
year, the members of the commission shall select one of its members to serve as
chair for the succeeding year and shall also appoint one of its members to
serve as secretary for the succeeding year.
   B.   Duties: It shall be the duty of the fair housing commission to:
      1.   Receive and investigate complaints charging unfair real estate
practices; and
      2.   Seek conciliation of such complaints, seek compliance by violators,
hold hearings, make findings of fact, issue recommendations and publish its
findings of fact and recommendations in accordance with the provisions of this
chapter. (Ord. 96, 6-24-1968)
5-4-6: GRIEVANCE PROCEDURE:
   A.   Complaint Filed: Any person aggrieved in any manner by an unfair real
estate practice may file a sworn written complaint with the commission setting
forth his grievance. Said complaint must be filed within thirty (30) days of
the commission of the alleged unfair real estate practice and shall state the
name and address of the complainant and of the person or persons against whom
the complaint is brought, and shall also state the alleged facts of the alleged
unfair real estate practice. A copy of said complaint shall be served on the
person complained against by certified or registered mail.
   B.   Investigation: After the filing of any complaint and service of a copy
of the complaint upon the person complained against, the chair of the
commission shall designate three (3) of the members to make an investigation in
connection therewith, and they shall file a written report of the results of
said investigation with the commission within twenty (20) days from the date of
their appointment. The commission may allow an additional twenty (20) day
period for investigation upon written application of the three (3) member
investigating committee filed within the original twenty (20) day period.
   C.   Remedies: If such three (3) members determine that probable cause
exists for crediting the alleged unfair real estate practice as a result of
said investigation, they shall immediately endeavor to eliminate the alleged
practice by conference, conciliation and persuasion.
   D.   Hearing:
      1.   In case of failure to eliminate such practice or in advance thereof,
if, in their judgment, circumstances so warrant, they shall send a written copy
of such complaint to all parties and at the same time notify them of a full
hearing of the alleged practice, at a time and place so specified in such
notice, which time shall not be less than ten (10) days following service of
the said notice. Following such notification, these three (3) members shall not
participate further in any action concerning the practice complained of, and
all future action shall be conducted by the remaining four (4) members of the
commission; provided, that the commissioners making such investigation are not
disqualified from testifying as any other witness.
      2.   Any real estate broker or other person charged with the unfair real
estate practice shall have the right to file an answer, and he and the
complainant may appear at the hearing in person, or be represented by counsel,
and submit testimony.
      3.   A copy of the complaint shall be mailed to the party complained
against prior to the hearing.
      4.   Such hearing shall be conducted by the four (4) members of the
commission who did not take part in the investigation. The commission shall not
be bound by the strict rules of evidence but shall decide the case in
accordance with the preponderance of the evidence, and which decision shall be
supported by substantial competent evidence. The commission shall have power to
administer oaths and to take sworn testimony.
      5.   At the conclusion of the hearing, the commission shall render a
written report and recommendations which shall be served by mail upon the
parties. No report shall be delayed more than sixty (60) days after the date of
the hearing. The commission shall keep a written record of the evidence of its
hearings. (Ord. 96, 6-24-1968)
5-4-7: SANCTIONS FOR VIOLATIONS:
At the conclusion of the hearing provided for in section
5-4-6 of this chapter, the commission may, as part of its findings, report and
order:
   A.   That no unfair housing practice has been proved and that no further
action is required.
   B.   Direct the city attorney to institute proceedings against any person
found to have committed an unfair real estate practice in violation of this
chapter. (Ord. 96, 6-24-1968)
5-4-8: OTHER PROCEEDINGS:
Nothing in this chapter shall be deemed to limit the right of the city or the
complainant to prosecute alleged violations of this chapter in the usual and
customary manner notwithstanding the fact that the investigating commissioners
determined that no probable cause existed for proceeding further with the
unfair housing practice or the fact that the commission may have decided
adversely to the complainant on his complaint. (Ord. 96, 6-24-1968)
5-4-9: PENALTY:
Any person committing an unfair real estate practice shall, upon conviction
thereof, be subject to a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 96, 6-24-1968; amd. 2008 Code)
CHAPTER 5
POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
5-5-1: Part Time Police
5-5-1: PART TIME POLICE:
   A.   Employment: The city of Leland Grove may employ part time police
officers from time to time as they deem necessary.
   B.   Duties: A part time police officer shall have all the responsibilities
of a full time police officer and such specific duties as delineated in the
general orders of the Leland Grove police department, but the number of hours a
part time officer may work within a calendar year is restricted. Part time
police officers shall not be assigned to supervise or direct full time police
officers. Part time police officers shall be trained in accordance with the
Illinois police training act 1  and the rules and requirements of the ILETSB as
now or hereafter amended.
   C.   Hiring Standards: Any person employed as a part time police officer
must meet the following standards:
      1.   Be of good moral character, of temperate habits, of sound health,
and physically and mentally able to perform assigned duties.
      2.   Be at least twenty one (21) years of age.
      3.   Pass a medical examination.
      4.   Possess a high school diploma or GED certificate.
      5.   Possess a valid state of Illinois driver's license.
      6.   Possess no prior felony convictions.
      7.   Any individual who has served in the U.S. military must have been
honorably discharged.
   D.   Discipline: Part time officers shall be under the disciplinary
jurisdiction of the chief of police. Part time police officers serve at the
discretion of the city authorities, shall not have any property rights in said
employment, shall only be entitled to the pay and benefits afforded part time
employees, and may be removed by the city authorities at any time. Part time
police officers shall comply with all applicable rules and general orders
issued by the police department. (Ord. 376, 2-28-2012)
 
Notes
1 1. 50 ILCS 705/1 et seq.
CHAPTER 6
LOCAL STATE OF EMERGENCY
SECTION:
5-6-1: Definitions
5-6-2: Declaration
5-6-3: Curfew Authorized
5-6-4: Orders Authorized
5-6-5: Duration
5-6-6: Notice
5-6-7: Violations
5-6-8: Effect On Other Ordinances
5-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have
the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context
clearly indicates a different meaning:
EMERGENCY: A riot or unlawful assembly characterized by the use of actual force
or
CURFEW: A prohibition against any person walking, running, loitering, standing
or motoring upon any alley, street, highway, public property or vacant premises
within the corporate limits of the city except officials of any governmental
unit and persons officially designated to duty with reference to said civil
emergency.
In addition to the definition specified above an emergency shall also be deemed
to exist if the conditions specified in the Illinois Emergency Management
Agency Act 20 ILCS 3305/4 as now or hereafter amended shall apply herein. (Ord.
440, 3-24-2020; Ord. 441, 4-28-2021)
5-6-2: DECLARATION:
Whenever an emergency, as defined in subsection (a) of this section exists, the
Mayor or designee is authorized to declare the existence of a local state of
emergency by means of a written declaration of the Mayor or designee, under
oath, setting forth the facts which constitute the emergency, describing the
nature of the emergency and declaring that a local state of emergency exists in
accordance with the definitions set forth in this section. This declaration
must be filed with the municipal clerk as soon as practicable after issuance.
(Ord. 440, 3-24-2020; Ord. 441, 4-28-2021)
5-6-3: CURFEW AUTHORIZED:
After proclamation of a local state of emergency by the Mayor, he or she may,
after consultation with the Council, order a general curfew applicable to such
geographical areas of the city or to the city as a whole, as he or she deems
reasonable and advisable, and applicable during such hours of the day or night
as he or she deems necessary in the interest of the public safety and welfare.
(Ord. 440, 3-24-2020; Ord. 441, 4-28-2021)
5-6-4: ORDERS AUTHORIZED:
After the proclamation of a local state of emergency, the Mayor may also, in
the interest of public safety and welfare, and to address this issues caused
threatened by the emergency, make take any or all of the following actions by
executive order during the state of emergency:
   A.   All actions reasonably necessary to sign contracts, hire temporary
workers, and make payment for services and equipment; or to conform with
emergency declarations made by County, State or Federal authorities to respond
to the emergency.
   B.   Approve previously appropriated expenditures of the city for the
purpose of continuing the operations of the municipality; and
   C.   In the event the local state of emergency extends beyond the current
fiscal year and a new budget has not been approved, the Mayor shall be
authorized  to approve new spending by the City during the existence of the
local state of emergency.
   D.   Order the discontinuance of selling, distributing, dispensing or giving
away of any firearms or ammunition of any character whatsoever. (Ord. 440, 3-
24-2020; Ord. 441, 4-28-2021)
5-6-5: DURATION:
The declaration herein authorized shall be effective for a period of up to
thirty one (31) days or until the adjournment of the next regular or special
meeting of the city council, whichever comes first, unless sooner terminated by
a proclamation of the Mayor, designee or, his or her interim emergency
successor, indicating that the civil emergency no longer exists. The Mayor or
his or her interim emergency successor, shall have the power, after approval of
the Council, to re-proclaim the existence of an emergency at the end of each
thirty one (31) days period during the time said emergency exists. (Ord. 440,
3-24-2020; Ord. 441, 4-28-2021)
5-6-6: NOTICE:
Upon issuing the proclamation herein authorized, the municipal clerk shall
notify the news media situated within the, and shall cause at least four copies
of the proclamation declaring the existence of the emergency and any curfew to
be posted at the following places within the city: the city hall, the police
station, the post office, and in the area of any curfew. (Ord. 440, 3-24-2020;
Ord. 441, 4-28-2021)
5-6-7: VIOLATIONS:
Any person violating the provisions of this section or executive orders issued
pursuant hereto shall be guilty of an offense against the City and shall be
punished as provided by section
4-1C-9 of the City code. (Ord. 440, 3-24-2020; Ord. 441, 4-28-2021)
5-6-8: EFFECT ON OTHER ORDINANCES:
Nothing contained in this section shall be construed to impair the powers
contained in this Code, giving powers to the police and fire departments, but
shall be construed together with existing ordinances now in effect for the
safety and welfare of the citizens of the City. (Ord. 440, 3-24-2020; Ord. 441,
4-28-2021)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL TRAFFIC PROVISIONS; DRIVING RULES
SECTION:
6-1-1: Through Streets
6-1-2: Stop Streets
6-1-3: One-Way Streets; Obedience To Traffic Control Devices
6-1-4: Speed Restrictions
6-1-5: Right Turn On Red Light At Chatham Road And Cherry Road
6-1-6: Reckless Driving; Driving Under Influence
6-1-7: Regulation Of Truck Vehicular Traffic
6-1-8: Road Closures
6-1-1: THROUGH STREETS:
   A.   Definition: For the purposes of this section, the term "motor vehicle"
shall be taken to mean and include every self-propelled device in, upon, or by
which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a highway.
   B.   Authority To Designate: The Mayor or anyone designated by the Mayor as
Road Commissioner, in order to regulate traffic, shall have the power to
designate certain streets as through streets and to erect stop signs at the
intersections of such designated through streets.
   C.   Stops Required: It shall be unlawful for any person driving a motor
vehicle to enter such designated through street, at which a stop sign has been
erected, without bringing such motor vehicle to a full and complete stop as
near the curb line of the through street as may be possible. (Ord. 28, 10-13-
1952)
   D.   Penalty: Any person who fails to comply with this section shall be
prosecuted and, upon conviction, shall be punished by a fine as provided in
section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 28, 10-13-1952; amd. 2008 Code)
6-1-2: STOP STREETS:
It shall be unlawful for the driver of any motor vehicle to drive into the
following intersections without first completely stopping his or her vehicle as
required by the City and State Statute. The stop signs provided for herein and
the installation thereof shall conform to the requirements of the "Uniform
Manual on Traffic Control Devices" published by the Illinois Department of
Transportation. Any person violating any provision of this section shall, upon
conviction, be punishable by a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (2008 Code)

6-1-3: ONE-WAY STREETS; OBEDIENCE TO TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to drive any vehicle in violation of
markings, signs, barriers, or other devices placed to designate streets, parts
of streets or specific lanes thereon upon which vehicular traffic shall proceed
in one direction during one period and the opposite direction during another
period of the day. (Ord. 321, 5-23-2000)
6-1-4: SPEED RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Reasonable And Proper Speed: No vehicle may be driven upon any street,
alley or highway at a speed which is greater than is reasonable and proper with
regard to traffic conditions and the use of the street, alley or highway, or
endangers the safety of any person or property. The fact that the speed of a
vehicle does not exceed the applicable maximum speed limit does relieve the
driver from the duty to decrease speed when approaching and crossing an
intersection, when approaching and going around a curve, when approaching a
hillcrest, when traveling upon any narrow or winding roadway, or when special
hazard exists with respect to pedestrians or other traffic or by reason of
weather or highway conditions. Speed must be decreased as may be necessary to
avoid colliding with any person or vehicle on or entering the street, alley or
highway in compliance with legal requirements and the duty of all persons to
use due care.
   B.   Statutory Speed Limits: No person may drive a vehicle upon any street,
alley or highway at a speed which is greater than the applicable statutory
maximum speed limit established by a regulation or ordinance.
   C.   Speed Limits Established:
      1.   Unless some other speed restriction is established by ordinance, the
maximum speed limit for all vehicles traveling within the boundaries of the
city is twenty five (25) miles per hour, except that section of Chatham Road
located within the boundaries of the city,  which shall have a speed limit of
thirty five (35) miles per hour.
      2.   The maximum speed limit for all vehicles traveling in an alley
located within the boundaries of the city is fifteen (15) miles per hour.
   D.   Alteration Of Speed Limits; Signs Posted: The mayor and the city
council may alter any speed restriction in subsection C of this section to a
higher or lower restriction, in which event, signs shall be posted upon such
street, alley or highway indicating the speed restriction. (Ord. 321, 5-23-
2000)
6-1-5: RIGHT TURN ON RED LIGHT AT CHATHAM ROAD AND CHERRY ROAD:
   A.   Right Turn Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for motor vehicle traffic
facing a steady red signal light at the intersection of Chatham Road and Cherry
Road, while proceeding in any direction on either street, to proceed into the
intersection for the purpose of making a right turn while such red light is
showing. At the intersection of Chatham Road and Cherry Road, motor vehicle
traffic approaching said intersection while facing a steady red signal light
alone must stop before entering the crosswalk on the near side of the
intersection and must remain stopped until a steady green signal light is
showing for the direction in which it is proceeding.
   B.   Signs Posted: An appropriate sign conforming to the uniform manual for
signs shall be erected at all four (4) corners of said intersection giving
notice of this regulation prohibiting right turns after stopping while facing a
steady red signal light. (Ord. 132, 2-25-1974)
   C.   Penalty: Any violation of this section shall be punishable by a fine as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 132, 2-25-1974; amd. 2008 Code)
6-1-6: RECKLESS DRIVING; DRIVING UNDER INFLUENCE:
   A.   Prohibited:
      1.   For the purpose of this subsection, the term "motor vehicle" shall
be taken to mean and include every self-propelled device in, upon, or by which
any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a highway. (Ord.
27, 10-13-1952)
      2.   No person shall drive or operate a motor vehicle upon any street,
highway, or alley within the limits of the city in a reckless, heedless, or
wanton manner, or while under the influence of any alcoholic beverage, other
drug or intoxicating compound.
      3.   Any person who shall violate any provisions of this subsection shall
be prosecuted therefor and, upon conviction, shall be punished by a fine as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 27, 10-13-1952; amd. 2008 Code)
   B.   Drug And Alcohol Testing: The chief of police is hereby authorized in
his or her discretion to request or direct the administration of chemical
analyses or other tests to determine the concentration of alcohol, other drug
or intoxicating compound in the breath, blood, urine, or other bodily substance
of any person arrested upon a charge of violation of 625 Illinois Compiled
Statutes 5/11-501, or any similar ordinance of the city. (Ord. 189, 12-28-1981;
amd. 2008 Code)
6-1-7: REGULATION OF TRUCK VEHICULAR TRAFFIC:
   A.   Purpose: The purpose of this section is to regulate and restrict by
classification vehicular traffic upon certain city streets in order to prevent
infrastructure damage, promote safe and efficient traffic flows, and preserve
the integrity and safety of the city's residential neighborhoods.
   B.   Definitions: The terms used in this section shall have the following
meanings unless otherwise specifically provided:
    ARTERIAL: Those roadways designated as arterial on the five (5) year
classification map for the Springfield area prepared by the Illinois department
of transportation.
   CITY: The city of Leland Grove.
   DESTINATION POINT: The fixed location that the operator of a vehicle must
directly access in order to load or unload goods, passengers or other cargo, or
to perform services.
   VEHICLE: Includes the motorized unit and any trailer or semitrailer attached
to the motorized unit.
   C.   Operation Limited To Designated Arterial Roadways: Except as otherwise
provided by this section, the operation of the following vehicles shall only
occur upon the designated arterial roadways in the city:
Any vehicle designed or used for the transportation of commodities, equipment
or materials, which vehicle:
      1.   Extends more than eight feet (8') to the rear of the driving or
passenger compartment of the vehicle;
      2.   Exceeds eight feet six inches (8'6") in width, and/or twenty six
feet (26') in length;
      3.   Exceeds eight thousand (8,000) pounds' (4 tons) gross weight,
including vehicle and maximum load; this includes all vehicles registered as a
motor vehicle of the second division except those in class B.
   D.   Exceptions: The prohibitions set forth in this section shall not apply
to the following:
      1.   The operation of a vehicle upon any street where directly and
unavoidably necessary in order to access or depart from a destination point.
When a destination point is not located immediately adjacent to an arterial
roadway, the vehicle operator shall access and/or depart from a destination
point using the shortest and most direct city route to and from the nearest
arterial roadway.
      2.   The operation of emergency and law enforcement vehicles.
      3.   The operation of any vehicle owned or operated by the city, a public
utility or any contractor, while directly engaged in the repair, maintenance or
construction of streets, street improvements or utilities within the city.
      4.   The operation of any vehicle within and pursuant to any officially
established temporary detour route.
      5.   The operation of any vehicle directly engaged in the collection and/
or transport of waste from city residences and businesses, including, but not
limited to, recyclable material.
      6.   The operation of passenger buses, including, but not limited to,
mass transit vehicles and school buses.
      7.   The operation of a vehicle otherwise permitted by this code to be
operated or parked at a residence by a resident.
   E.   Enforcement; Penalty: Any person, firm or corporation who violates any
provision of this section shall be punished by a fine not to exceed three
hundred dollars ($300.00). (Ord. 397, 6-24-2014)
6-1-8: ROAD CLOSURES:
   A.   Purpose: The City Council finds that the closing of Greenbriar and
Huntleigh Roads at the City's Municipal boundaries is a public purpose that is
necessary to protect the public health, safety, and welfare of the City, its
residents and all persons using the City's streets. In addition, the closing of
Greenbriar and Huntleigh Roads at the City's Municipal boundaries serves a wide
variety of functions that promote the purposes of this section. These functions
include, without limitation, each of the following:
      1.   Enhancing public safety by reducing vehicular traffic on roadways,
which have no sidewalks, curbs or street lights.
      2.   Enhancing public safety and controlling road maintenance costs of
the City by reducing vehicular traffic on roadways, thus slowing the
deterioration of asphalt pavements and oil and chip pavements.
      3.   Enhancing public safety and controlling police costs of the City by
reducing vehicular traffic on roadways, thus permitting City police to engage
in other public safety activities.
   B.   Definitions:
    AFFECTED STREETS: Greenbriar and Huntleigh Roads.
   PERSON: Any individual, corporation, partnership, association, or other
legal entity.
   PUBLIC SERVICE VEHICLE: Any State, County and Municipal law enforcement
vehicle, Municipal Fire Department vehicle, public or private ambulance
vehicle, or any other emergency service vehicle, and includes school buses and
licensed waste haulers.
   C.   Closing Of Greenbriar And Huntleigh Roads:
      1.   From and after the effective date of this section, the affected
streets will be closed to vehicular traffic by any person, except a public
service vehicle, at the point on the street closest to the Municipal boundary
of the City of Leland Grove, Illinois, as determined by the Mayor and the City
Road Commissioner.
      2.   The appropriate means by which the closure of the affected streets
will be undertaken, including the necessary signage indicating the closure will
be determined by the Mayor and the City Council.
      3.   The total cost to be incurred for the closure of the affected
streets shall not be more than the amount budgeted, as set forth in the most
recent budget approved or as such may be modified with the approval of the City
Council. (Ord. 347, 9-27-2005)
CHAPTER 2
PARKING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-2-1: Application Of Parking Ordinances
6-2-2: Method Of Parking
6-2-3: Parking Not To Obstruct Traffic
6-2-4: Parking Regulated
6-2-5: Parking Prohibited At Certain Places
6-2-6: Parking Prohibited During Certain Hours
6-2-7: Parking Prohibited On Specific Streets
6-2-8: Enforcement And Penalty
6-2-9: Administrative Towing Fee
6-2-10: Vehicles Subject To Seizure And Impoundment
6-2-11: Towing And Storage Fees
6-2-12: Procedure For Seizure And Impoundment Of Vehicles
6-2-13: Notice And Opportunity For Hearing
6-2-14: Administrative Hearings For Impoundment And Release Of Vehicles
6-2-1: APPLICATION OF PARKING ORDINANCES:
The provisions of any ordinances prohibiting the stopping, standing or parking
of vehicles shall apply at all times or at those times therein specified or as
indicated on official signs except when it is necessary to stop a vehicle to
avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with the directions of a
police officer, authorized personnel or official traffic control device. (Ord.
324, 3-27-2001)
6-2-2: METHOD OF PARKING:
No person shall stand or park a vehicle in a roadway other than parallel with
the edge of the roadway headed in the direction of lawful traffic movement and
with the curbside wheels of the vehicle within twelve inches (12") of the curb
or edge of the roadway, except as otherwise provided in this chapter. (Ord.
324, 3-27-2001; amd. 2008 Code)
6-2-3: PARKING NOT TO OBSTRUCT TRAFFIC:
No person shall park any vehicle upon a street in a manner or under conditions
as to leave available less than fifteen feet (15') of the width of the roadway
for free movement of vehicular traffic on a two-way street or less than ten
feet (10') of the width of the roadway for free movement of vehicular traffic
on a one-way street. (Ord. 324, 3-27-2001)
6-2-4: PARKING REGULATED:
When signs have been erected upon any street indicating that stopping, standing
or parking is prohibited during designated hours or is permitted for a
specified period of time, no person shall park any vehicle on the street in
violation of the sign. (Ord. 324, 3-27-2001)
6-2-5: PARKING PROHIBITED AT CERTAIN PLACES:
The operator of any vehicle shall not stop, stand or park a vehicle in any of
the following places, except when necessary in an emergency to avoid conflict
with other traffic or in compliance with directions of a police officer,
authorized personnel, or official traffic sign or signal, or city ordinance.
For the purpose of this section, "official signs" shall mean all signs,
markings and devices which conform with the state manual and not inconsistent
with city ordinances, placed or erected by authority of the city for the
purpose of regulating, warning and controlling parking. Violations may be
charged as specified in section
6-2-8 of this chapter.
   A.   Within an intersection.
   B.   Upon a crosswalk.
   C.   Upon any bridge or other elevated structure upon a highway or within a
highway tunnel.
   D.   Between a safety zone and the adjacent curb or within thirty feet (30')
of a point of the curb immediately opposite the end of a safety zone.
   E.   Within thirty feet (30') of a traffic signal, beacon or sign on the
approaching side.
   F.   Within twenty feet (20') of any intersection or crosswalk.
   G.   Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant.
   H.   Within fifty feet (50') of the nearest rail of a railroad grade
crossing.
   I.   Within twenty feet (20') of the driveway entrance to any fire
department station and on the side of the street opposite the entrance to any
such station, within seventy five feet (75') of such entrance, when properly
signposted.
   J.   On a sidewalk or parkway.
   K.   On any properly designated and marked fire or emergency lane.
   L.   On any public street or portion thereof at any time when such street is
being cleaned and which has been posted as such.
   M.   In any posted curb loading zone.
   N.   In any public alley, except for the purpose of loading or unloading
merchandise; provided that the flow of traffic in the alley may not be blocked
nor the vehicle left unattended.
   O.   In any bus stop; provided that vehicles other than buses may drive to
the curb at a bus stop for the purpose of receiving or discharging passengers.
   P.   In any traffic lane; provided that a vehicle may be stopped briefly
within a traffic lane for the purpose of receiving or discharging passengers.
   Q.   On the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or
curb of a street.
   R.   On any snow emergency route during a state of emergency as declared by
the city.
   S.   On any street adjacent to school property or playgrounds when official
signs are erected.
   T.   On any property owned by the city and used for the transaction of
public business when official signs are erected; provided, however, this
prohibition shall not apply to city owned vehicles operating in an emergency or
with prior approval from the city.
   U.   In front of a public or private driveway except briefly to pick up or
discharge passengers.
   V.   Alongside or opposite any street excavation or obstruction when
stopping, standing or parking would obstruct traffic.
   W.   On any railroad tracks. A violation of any part of this subsection
shall result in a mandatory fine of five hundred dollars ($500.00) or fifty
(50) hours of community service.
   X.   On any controlled access highway.
   Y.   In the area between roadways of a divided highway, including
crossovers.
   Z.   At any place where official signs prohibit parking. (Ord. 324, 3-27-
2001; amd. 2008 Code)
6-2-6: PARKING PROHIBITED DURING CERTAIN HOURS:
No person shall stop, stand or park any vehicle on any street or alley between
the hours of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. of any day,
except in an emergency. (Ord. 324, 3-27-2001)
6-2-7: PARKING PROHIBITED ON SPECIFIC STREETS:
No person shall park a vehicle, except when necessary to avoid conflict with
other traffic or in compliance with the directions of a police officer or
traffic control device, along the following streets. Appropriate signs shall be
erected designating the areas as no parking zones. Any person violating this
section shall, upon conviction, be punishable by a fine of not more than two
hundred fifty dollars ($250.00). (2008 Code)
 
Street           Location                   Sides          Ordinance No.
