of the county recorder of deeds, together with any necessary lien subordination
agreement.
      2.   If the final plat is not recorded within one year after approval by
the city council, the plat must be resubmitted to the city council to determine
whether any adjustments in the final plat are needed to meet changes that have
occurred in and near the plat area that would affect the proper functioning of
the subdivision. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
CHAPTER 3
DESIGN AND IMPROVEMENT STANDARDS
SECTION:
10-3-1: Improvement Standards And Specifications
10-3-2: Streets
10-3-3: Lots And Blocks
10-3-4: Utility Easements
10-3-5: Storm Water Control
10-3-6: Sidewalks
10-3-7: Sanitary Sewers
10-3-8: Water Supply
10-3-9: Backfill Over Underground Utilities
10-3-10: Street Lighting
10-3-1: IMPROVEMENT STANDARDS AND SPECIFICATIONS:
Unless stated otherwise in this title, all construction shall be performed in
accordance with the state "Standard Specifications For Road And Bridge
Construction", adopted July 1, 1976, or the latest revised edition adopted by
the state department of transportation and the city council. (Ord. 212, 6-22-
1985)
10-3-2: STREETS:
   A.   Right Of Way Widths:
      1.   The minimum width of a street right of way in any subdivision shall
not be less than the following:
 
Major thoroughfare       120 feet
Secondary thoroughfare   80 feet
Collector street         60 feet
Minor residential street 50 feet
Alley                    20 feet
 
      2.   For subdivisions that adjoin existing streets, additional right of
way shall be dedicated, as needed, to meet the above requirements. This shall
be done as follows:
         a.   The entire additional right of way shall be provided when the
subdivision is located on both sides of the existing street.
         b.   One-half (1/2) of the required right of way shall be provided
when the subdivision is located on only one side of the existing street.
      3.   In no instance shall the resulting right of way width be less than
fifty feet (50').
   B.   Design: The following requirements shall be incorporated into the
design of all streets:
      1.   Vertical Alignment:
         a.   Grades: The maximum grade on a major thoroughfare shall be five
percent (5%). The maximum grade on all other streets shall be eight percent
(8%). The minimum grade on all streets shall be 0.40 percent. All street grades
will be subject to the approval of the city engineer.
         b.   Vertical Curves: All grade changes shall be connected by vertical
curves. The lengths of vertical curves on major thoroughfares shall not be less
than thirty (30) times the algebraic difference in rates of grade, and not less
than fifteen (15) times the algebraic difference in rates of grade on all other
streets. The minimum length of vertical curves on all types of streets shall be
ten feet (10').
      2.   Horizontal Alignment:
         a.   Horizontal Curves: When a centerline deflection angle is greater
than two degrees (2°), the following curves will be required in the street:
Secondary and major thoroughfares shall have a minimum centerline radius of
three hundred feet (300') and a minimum length of curve of one hundred feet
(100'); all other types of streets shall have a minimum centerline radius of
one hundred feet (100') except when the deflection angle exceeds sixty degrees
(60°), in which case, a minimum centerline radius of fifty feet (50') may be
used. The pavement in all cases shall be wide enough to allow the movement of a
WB-50 design vehicle, as described in the state department of transportation
design manual.
         b.   Intersections: The use of "T" intersections is encouraged, and
all street intersections shall be as nearly at right angles as possible, and in
no instance less than sixty degrees (60°). The back of curb radius at
intersections shall not be less than twenty feet (20').
         c.   Street Offsets: Street centerline offsets shall not be less than
one hundred twenty five feet (125'), unless otherwise warranted to the
satisfaction of the city engineer. This requirement will not be altered for
secondary or major thoroughfares.
      3.   Pavement Design:
         a.   The pavement thickness will be designed in accordance with the
latest edition or revision thereof of the design manual of the state department
of transportation bureau of design.
         b.   The average daily traffic (ADT) used in the above design will be
determined by the engineer for the subdivision and approved by the city
engineer.
         c.   The Illinois bearing ratio (IBR) used in the above design will be
furnished by the subdivider with supporting evidence indicating the soil
classifications, location of boring, boring depth and a standard proctor test.
         d.   The minimum pavement design shall be one of the following: two
inches (2") bituminous concrete surface course, class I on four inches (4")
bituminous aggregate material (BAM, 1200 MS), or six inches (6") unreinforced
Portland cement concrete pavement. Alternative designs may be submitted to the
city engineer for consideration.
      4.   Pavement Construction:
         a.   All streets shall be constructed in accordance with the latest
edition of the state "Standard Specifications For Road And Bridge
Construction".
         b.   Before pavement construction can begin, the entire subgrade shall
be compacted to not less than ninety five percent (95%) of the standard
laboratory density. Densities shall be determined as provided in article 207.05
of the state "Standard Specifications For Road And Bridge Construction" or the
latest revision thereof. The number of density tests required shall be
determined by the city engineer.
         c.   If it is found that the subgrade cannot be compacted, it should
be removed and replaced with suitable materials. The depth to which this
unsuitable material is replaced shall be determined by the city engineer.
         d.   The pavement design as described above is subject to the IBR
value of the new materials.
         e.   Pavement construction should be completed without delay and
should be closed to traffic until the surface is complete. Concrete pavement
should be closed to traffic for fourteen (14) days after placement or seven (7)
days with a modulus of rupture of six hundred fifty (650) pounds per square
inch. The density of the compacted bituminous mixture shall be determined as
outlined in section 406.15 of the state "Standard Specifications For Road And
Bridge Construction".
      5.   Pavement Width: The minimum pavement width shall be thirty one feet
(31') from back of curb to back of curb. Where high volume traffic is
anticipated, a wider pavement will be required. The width of this wider
pavement will be determined by the engineer for the subdivision and the city
engineer.
      6.   Curb And Gutter:
         a.   The standard curb and gutter required adjacent to flexible
pavement shall be a mountable type with the following dimensions: twenty four
inches (24") wide, eight inches (8") thick on the front face (pavement side),
ten inches (10") thick on the back face, seven inches (7") thick at the
centerline (flow line), and a ten inch (10") radius in the flow line. The curb
and gutter adjacent to concrete pavement, if poured monolithically, may be
limited to the thickness of the pavement. When poured separately, curb bars
should be placed in the pavement in accordance with the state "Standard
Specifications For Road And Bridge Construction" and should be poured to full
thickness as described above.
         b.   In subdivisions proposed to have streets with an anticipated
average daily traffic volume of two thousand five hundred (2,500) or more, a
barrier type curb and gutter similar to type B6.18 as described in the state
department of transportation "Highway Standards" shall be used. Other locations
where a barrier type curb and gutter are required will be determined by the
engineer for the subdivision and the city engineer.
      7.   Pavement Crown: The minimum crown used on all pavements shall be
one-fourth inch (1/4") per foot measured from the edge of the pavement to the
centerline of the street. Concrete pavement with an integral curb shall have a
minimum crown of three-eighths inch (3/8") per foot.
      8.   Dead End Streets:
         a.   Minor residential streets that are also dead end streets shall be
no more than six hundred feet (600') long unless necessitated by topography. A
turnaround shall be provided at the closed end having an outside roadway
diameter of at least eighty feet (80') and a street right of way diameter of
one hundred feet (100').
         b.   Where it is necessary to provide for street access to adjoining
property not yet subdivided, proposed streets shall be extended by dedication
to the boundary of such unsubdivided property. Such temporary dead end streets
in excess of two hundred fifty feet (250') in length shall be provided with a
temporary T turnaround or a temporary cul-de-sac. The type of construction
shall be determined by the city engineer. At the end of all streets temporarily
dead ended, a barricade meeting the provisions of the "Illinois Manual On
Uniform Traffic Control Devices" shall be installed.
      9.   Restriction Of Access: When a subdivision or portion thereof adjoins
a major or secondary thoroughfare, no lot shall have direct access thereto.
These lots shall be provided access to another street and shall have adequate
depth for screen planting on the portion of any lot contiguous to the major or
secondary thoroughfare.
      10.   Street Names And Signs:
         a.   Street Names: A proposed street that is in alignment with and/or
joins an existing named street shall bear the name of the existing street. In
no case shall the proposed name of a street duplicate the name of an existing
street within the plat jurisdiction of this title. The use of the suffix
"street", "avenue", "boulevard", "driveway", "place", or "court" or similar
description shall not be a distinction sufficient to constitute compliance with
this subsection B10a.
         b.   Street Name Signs: Street name signs shall be erected at all
intersections by and at the expense of the subdivider and shall be subject to
the specifications of the city engineer.
      11.   Private Streets: There shall be no private streets platted in any
subdivision. Every subdivision lot shall be served from a publicly dedicated
street.
      12.   Alleys: Alleys are not recommended in residential subdivisions
unless deemed necessary by the city engineer.
      13.   Ramps: Where sidewalks cross a barrier type curb and gutter, ramps
shall be constructed to accommodate the handicapped. These ramps shall be
constructed to the lines and grades shown on the standard sidewalk ramp example
available at the city engineer's office. Inlets for storm drainage shall not be
located so that a pedestrianway will be interrupted by the inlet grating. Other
locations where these ramps are required will be determined by the city
engineer.
      14.   Seeding Or Sodding: When areas are found to be especially
susceptible to erosion, the city engineer may require control measures
including, but not limited to, sodding, diversions, temporary or permanent
vegetation, mulching, bench terraces, outlet channels, grade stabilization
structures, bank erosion structures, and sediment basins or traps. (Ord. 212,
6-22-1985)
10-3-3: LOTS AND BLOCKS:
   A.   Size Of Blocks: Blocks in residential subdivisions are recommended to
be not less than four hundred feet (400') nor more than one thousand two
hundred feet (1,200') in length measured along the greatest dimension of the
enclosed block area. In blocks over eight hundred feet (800') in length, the
city council may require one or more public crosswalks, with a right of way of
not less than ten feet (10') in width, to extend entirely across the block at
locations deemed necessary at intervals not closer than four hundred feet
(400').
   B.   Lot Arrangement:
      1.   Side lot lines shall be at right angles to straight street lines or
substantially radial to curved street lines. However, for the purposes of solar
orientation, side lot lines need not be at right angles to straight street
lines or radial to curved street lines; provided, that side lot lines run
within twenty degrees (20°) east or west from due north to due south. In the
latter case, street layout and building setbacks should also be designed so
that at least eighty percent (80%) of the buildings in the subdivision can be
oriented with their long axis running from east to west, with a possible
variation of twenty degrees (20°) to the southeast and twenty degrees (20°) to
the southwest.
      2.   Each lot must front upon a public street with at least fifty feet
(50') of right of way width. Blocks must fit readily into the overall plan of
the subdivision, and the design must evidence consideration of lot planning,
easy traffic circulations (both vehicular and pedestrian), and provide space
for public land use as may be needed in the neighborhood.
      3.   Individuals desiring access to existing township roads must obtain
the approval of the appropriate township highway commissioner with respect to
the type and size of culvert to be utilized.
   C.   Public Use And Service Areas:
      1.   Due consideration shall be given to the allocation of areas suitably
located and of adequate size for playgrounds and parks for local or
neighborhood use as well as public service areas.
      2.   When a proposed school, neighborhood park, electric substation,
water storage tank, recreation area, or public access to water frontage is
located in whole or in part in a proposed subdivision, the city council may
require, as a condition of final plat approval, that such space within the
subdivision be reserved and not developed for a period not to exceed one year
from the date of such final plat approval. Within the one year period, the
appropriate public agency may acquire the reserved property in the manner
provided by law and before it is developed. If the reserved site is not
acquired and no legal action is filed by the appropriate public agency within
the one year period, the reservation shall become void, and the site previously
reserved may then be used for other purposes. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
   D.   Survey Monuments:
      1.   All survey monuments shall be located and be made of the appropriate
material as stated in chapter 765 of the Illinois Compiled Statutes. (Ord. 212,
6-22-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
      2.   References must be made upon the plat to known and permanent
monuments from which future survey may be made, and the surveyor must, at the
time of making his survey, set, in such manner that they will not be moved by
frost, good and sufficient monuments marking the external boundaries of the
tract to be divided or subdivided and must designate upon the plat the points
where they may be found. These monuments must be placed at all corners, at each
end of all curves, at the point where a curve changes its radius, at all angle
points in any line and at all angle points along a meander line, the points to
be not less than twenty feet (20') back from the normal water elevation of a
lake or from the bank of a stream; except, that when such corners or points
fall within a street, or proposed future street, the monuments must be placed
in the right of way line of the street. All internal boundaries, corners and
points must be monumented in the field by like monuments as defined above.
These monuments, two (2) of which must be of stone or reinforced concrete, must
be set at the opposite extremities of the property platted, placed at all block
corners, at each end of all curves, at the points where a curve changes its
radius, and at all angle points in any line. All lots must be monumented in the
field at all corners.
   E.   Lot Grading:
      1.   All grading between the right of way lines shall be completed to the
lines and grades shown on the grading sheets in the construction plans.
      2.   The full width of the right of way shall be graded including the
subgrade of the areas to be paved.
      3.   All stumps and trees that cannot be saved, along with boulders and
similar items shall be removed.
      4.   All grading in the subdivision shall be related to the topography of
the surrounding area. All street embankments shall be raised at least one and
one-half feet (11/2') above the high water elevation.
      5.   All building lots shall be graded or have natural slopes that will
properly allow surface drainage to flow away from the principal structures to
be located on the lot.
      6.   Grading in the subdivision shall provide alternate drainageways for
the purpose of carrying water away from homes and preventing damage during
periods of heavy rainfall. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
10-3-4: UTILITY EASEMENTS:
   A.   General Requirements:
      1.   All utilities must be constructed and installed underground. Utility
easements shall be provided along front, rear or side lot lines for the purpose
of erecting and maintaining one or more of the following facilities: storm
sewers, sanitary sewers, surface drainage, gas mains, water mains, and
underground electric lines, telephone lines, cable television and such other
utilities reasonably required for an urban structure. Easements shall normally
be a minimum of ten feet (10') in width except where they are needed for only
one facility such as an underground street lighting cable where six feet (6')
is sufficient. Nothing contained herein shall preclude the location of a
utility in the street if the respective company so desires.
      2.   Alternate locations for various utilities shall be decided upon by
the appropriate utility companies, subject to the approval of the city
engineer. In no case shall trees, permanent buildings or other manmade
improvements that obstruct surface drainage be placed on rear and side lot
easements.
      3.   It is the responsibility of the subdivider to notify all utility
companies in writing when the land to be developed has been graded in
accordance with the approved construction plans and is ready for installation
of a given utility.
   B.   Ten Foot Easements: When an easement will not include sanitary sewer or
surface drainage systems, a ten foot (10') easement width shall be sufficient
and the utilities located as follows:
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/40450415285a20d54eca53fd28c1446d8d3313de/
IMAGES/0-0-0-751.gif]
 
   C.   Fifteen Foot Easements: When an easement will include either a sanitary
sewer system or a surface drainage system, but not both systems, a fifteen foot
(15') easement shall be required and the utilities located as follows:
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/40450415285a20d54eca53fd28c1446d8d3313de/
IMAGES/0-0-0-753.gif]
 
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/40450415285a20d54eca53fd28c1446d8d3313de/
IMAGES/0-0-0-755.gif]
 
   D.   Twenty Foot Easements: When a utility easement will include both a
sanitary sewer system and a surface drainage system, a twenty foot (20')
easement shall be required and the utilities located as follows:
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/40450415285a20d54eca53fd28c1446d8d3313de/
IMAGES/0-0-0-757.gif]
 
   E.   Ten Foot Access Easement:
      1.   When sanitary or storm sewers are located in the back yard, a ten
foot (10') easement in the side yard will be required from the street right of
way to each manhole or inlet.
      2.   Other combinations of utilities or the inclusion of water mains or
gas mains in a rear yard easement will require a different easement design than
is shown above. When water mains and gas mains are to be located in the street
right of way, the gas main should be installed along the north and west curb
line of the street and the water main placed along the south and east curb
line. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
10-3-5: STORM WATER CONTROL:
   A.   All subdivisions within the jurisdictional limits of the city shall be
provided with adequate facilities for control of storm water runoff. These
storm water improvements consisting of storm sewers and/or open channels,
inlets, catch basins, manholes and a combination of temporary storage and
controlled release of storm water runoff shall be designed and constructed to
conform with standards established by the city engineer and shall adequately
drain the area being developed and also all of such other areas which naturally
drain through the area being developed. It is intended that the maximum
controlled release rate from any subdivision shall not exceed the natural safe
storm water drainage capacity of the downstream storm water drainage system as
defined in this title. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
   B.   It is anticipated in this title that a landowner shall be allowed to
let existing excess storm water runoff from tributary areas upstream from that
owner's land pass through without storage or controlled release of such runoff.
It is further anticipated that this title will require the controlled release
of excess storm water runoff resulting from development of the owner's land.
The controlled release rate of excess storm water runoff from an owner's land
shall not exceed the rate of runoff which would have occurred from that owner's
land prior to the development of that owner's land. It is presumed that prior
to development, that owner's land had a traditional agricultural use. It is
further presumed that the maximum safe storm water drainage capacity for
downstream storm water systems is the capacity required to carry a rate of
storm water runoff from a 5-year return period storm prior to the effective
date hereof. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
   C.   The following requirements shall be applicable and shall be satisfied
prior to the construction, improvement or development of any structure, project
or land which is subject to the provisions of this title:
      1.   The maximum controlled release rate for independent watershed areas
within the owner's land shall be determined in the following manner:
         a.   For that portion of the watershed outside of an owner's land, the
peak rate of runoff which would have occurred for a 5-year return period storm
under the state of development existing just prior to application for
development of an owner's land shall be calculated and determined.
         b.   For that portion of the watershed within the lands of an owner,
the peak rate of runoff which would have occurred for a 5-year return period
storm under a state of traditional agricultural usage shall be calculated and
determined.
         c.   The maximum controlled release rate for each independent
watershed area within the owner's land as it exits the owner's land for storms
up to and including the 100-year return period storm shall be the sum of
subsections C1a and C1b of this section.
         d.   The peak rate of runoff which would have occurred for a 5-year
return period storm shall be determined using the rational method or other
substantial method acceptable to the city engineer.
         e.   The 5-year and 50-year return period storm shall be determined
utilizing the most recently available information.
         f.   In the event that the downstream storm water runoff drainage
system is inadequate to accommodate the maximum release rate provided above,
then the city, at its option, may reduce the allowable release rate to that
rate permitted by the capacity of the receiving storm water runoff drainage
system and additional storage as determined by the city engineer may be
required to store that portion of the runoff exceeding the capacity of the
receiving storm water runoff drainage system.
      2.   Unless engineering evidence is presented to the city engineer
warranting exceptions, storm sewers which will drain twenty (20) acres or less
for residential development will be designed and constructed to meet the
following criteria (specific information will be obtained from the city
engineer for all other areas):
         a.   All improvements will be designed to handle runoff from a storm
having a 5-year frequency. Storm water conduit drains that discharge to open
channels shall terminate with suitable outlet structures to control soil
erosion and to prevent progressive failure of the conduit in an upstream
direction.
         b.   Inlets and/or catch basins shall be spaced so that water will not
flow over land more than five hundred feet (500') and shall be so located that
in no case will water be required to flow across a street or be retained
outside the center ten feet (10') of the drainage utility easement. Limited
temporary surface storage or runoff from storms exceeding the design frequency
may be permitted, subject to the approval of the city engineer. Inlets covered
by a metal grate should have a grate of a type that will not be hazardous to
bicyclists.
         c.   Storm sewer slopes shall be such that a minimum velocity of two
and one-half feet (21/2') per second is maintained when the pipe is flowing
full without surcharge. In cases where it is impractical to obtain the above
minimum velocity, modification shall be subject to approval by the city
engineer. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
         d.   Manholes with a minimum diameter of four feet (4') with cast iron
frames and grates meeting city standards shall be installed at any abrupt
change in direction, size, or grade of the sewer and at all other locations
necessary to limit the distance between manholes to four hundred feet (400'). A
greater distance will be allowed if it makes the manhole more accessible. This
greater distance is subject to the approval of the city engineer. (Ord. 212, 6-
22-1985; amd. 2008 Code)
         e.   Joints for storm sewer conduit may be mortar joints or bituminous
joints complying with paragraph 30.3.02B or paragraph 30.3.02C, respectively,
as specified in the "Standard Specifications For Water And Sewer Main
Construction In Illinois", second edition, dated November 1973, or the latest
revision thereof.
         f.   When storm sewers are located in the back yard easement, each
inlet shall be located on or in line with the side property line common to the
access easement.
         g.   It will be the responsibility of the subdivider to provide grade
control for rear lot drainage to each lot owner. It will be the lot owner's
responsibility to maintain the drainage course and to keep it free from
features that restrict natural drainage. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
10-3-6: SIDEWALKS:
Concrete sidewalks at least four feet (4') wide and four inches (4") thick
shall be constructed on both sides of each street at least four and one-half
feet (41/2') from and at least four inches (4") above the backs of the curbs.
They shall be located one foot (1') inside the street right of way. However,
the city council may waive or reduce this requirement if it is established that
the reasonable anticipated growth of the area and the probable nature of its
development, its distance from concentrated urban development and developments
creating pedestrian travel and the estimated volume of vehicular travel on the
streets make such sidewalks unnecessary for the protection of the public safety
and welfare. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
10-3-7: SANITARY SEWERS:
   A.   Separate Services Required: Sanitary sewers shall be constructed
throughout the entire subdivision in such a manner as to serve adequately each
building lot with a connection thereto.
   B.   Location: When possible, public sanitary sewers shall be located in the
north or west boulevard (between curb and sidewalk) within the street right of
way or in a fifteen foot (15') easement behind the sidewalk within the house
setback area. Parallel sewer lines along the street may be used. Manholes shall
be installed on side property lines. Sanitary sewers may be located in back
yard easements when the line is completely accessible from the downstream
manhole in the public street. This line cannot be more than five hundred feet
(500') in length. Rear yard locations can be designated only with the approval
of the city engineer.
   C.   Discharge Of Storm Water Prohibited: Under no circumstances will the
entrance of storm water to the sanitary sewers be permitted. The words "storm
water" shall be interpreted to include water from roof downspouts, basement
footing perimeter drains, yard drains, and ground water as well as surface
runoff.
   D.   Compliance With City, Sanitary District And State Requirements: All
sanitary sewer connections and disposal systems shall comply with the
ordinances of the city, the Springfield sanitary district and the requirements
of the state environmental protection agency.
   E.   Construction Specifications: Construction features and details for
sanitary sewers and appurtenances shall comply with the "Standard
Specifications For Water And Sewer Main Construction In Illinois", dated
November 1973, or the latest revision thereof.
   F.   Manholes:
      1.   Manholes on sanitary sewers shall be located at the beginning and
ending of all sewer runs and at changes in slope, size, and direction. The
distance between manholes shall not exceed four hundred feet (400'), except in
locations where a greater distance will make the manholes more accessible. This
greater distance is subject to the approval of the city engineer.
      2.   Manholes shall be constructed of masonry units having an internal
diameter of not less than four feet (4'), fitted with cast iron frames, covers
and steps.
   G.   House Service Lines:
      1.   A house service sewer line having an internal diameter of not less
than six inches (6") for a multiple-family dwelling or commercial building and
four inches (4") for a single-family dwelling shall be provided from all main
sewers constructed in the street right of way to the adjacent property line of
each lot in the subdivision. A house service sewer line having an internal
diameter of not less than six inches (6") shall be provided from the main sewer
of all sewers run on easements or for a distance of five feet (5') beyond the
easements into the adjacent lot.
      2.   Each such house service line shall be adequately plugged with a
suitable disc or stopper at the end of such line to make the joint formed
completely watertight. Service line construction shall be equivalent to the
requirements for main collecting sanitary sewers.
      3.   The lowest sanitary sewer outlet elevation from a residence shall be
according to the standards of the Springfield sanitary district.
   H.   Tests: Upon completion of the sewer construction, an air test,
infiltration test or exfiltration test, as may be appropriate, shall be
conducted on the entire sewer system before any building is allowed to connect
to the system. The test shall be conducted under the supervision of a
registered professional engineer. The engineer shall furnish a certified copy
of the test results to the city engineer and the district engineer of the
Springfield sanitary district before connection of service lines. (Ord. 212, 6-
22-1985)
10-3-8: WATER SUPPLY:
   A.   The installation and sterilization of all water mains shall be in
accordance with the "Standard Specifications For Water And Sewer Main
Construction In Illinois" and must be approved by the city engineer.
   B.   When the subdivision is to be served by a public water system, water
mains not less than six inches (6") in diameter shall be constructed throughout
the entire subdivision, and larger diameter water mains shall be installed if
needed to provide the area fire flow required by the insurance services office
guide for determination of required fire flow. Fire hydrants shall be installed
throughout the entire system at intervals of not more than five hundred feet
(500') and shall be less if required by the fire safety division of the
department of public health and safety of the city of Springfield, with shutoff
valves at each hydrant. All fire hydrants shall be provided with two (2) to
three inch (3") nozzles with Springfield fire department threads and one to
four inch (4") steamer nozzle with Springfield fire department threads, and
shall have flow characteristics similar to those of a five and one-fourth inch
(51/4") hydrant valve.
   C.   Every water supply system shall be designed in such a manner as to
provide an area fire flow which will meet the requirements established by the
fire safety division of the Springfield fire department or the appropriate fire
agency serving the area. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
10-3-9: BACKFILL OVER UNDERGROUND UTILITIES:
   A.   Where an underground utility is to be placed in an area which has a
permanent type street or sidewalk surface or upon which such a surface is to be
constructed within a period of one year, the backfill above the utility, or in
the case of sewers, to the level of the bottom of the permanent type surface,
shall be made with material specified by "Selected Granular Backfill" as
provided for above the top of the gravel cradle in the "Standards And
Specifications For Water And Sewer Main Construction In Illinois", dated
September 1978, or the latest revision thereof. In areas not now subject to
vehicular traffic, nor, in the opinion of the city engineer, likely to be
within a period of one year, backfills may be made with selected excavation
material, free from clods and stones, provided such trench backfill is
adequately jetted from the bottom up, completely filling the trench immediately
after backfilling. Compaction of all backfill material shall be done by one of
the following methods:
      1.   Backfill shall be placed in layers not exceeding twelve inches (12")
in depth, each layer to be thoroughly tamped to the satisfaction of the city
engineer.
      2.   Backfill shall be jetted to the satisfaction of the city engineer.
After jetting, such settlement as may have occurred shall be filled with
surplus material.
   B.   Before utilities are installed, the subdivider shall certify to the
utility company that the finished grade elevation has been constructed where
the utilities are to be placed.
   C.   Where possible, underground utilities shall be installed prior to
pavement and sidewalk construction. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
10-3-10: STREET LIGHTING:
Streetlights shall be provided along public streets conforming to current IES
standard RP-8 or ANSI standard D12.1. (Ord. 212, 6-22-1985)
